(3) Zheng Zhaoxi, Deputy Chief of Staff, and Wu Jialu, Director of the said Rear Headquarters, shall be mutually responsible for handling the liaison matters of all official documents between the front and rear headquarters on a daily basis to avoid conflicts. (4) All military orders within Hunan Province shall be handled by the Hunan Provincial Security Headquarters. (September 14)

Waves of Factional Strife in Hunan 79

The Pi Dao Faction and the Zuan Zi Faction Mutually Exclude Each Other; Huang Jiasheng Laments the Decline of Party Morality

Changsha Correspondence: In Hunan Province, party affairs have been at a standstill for several months due to the rift between the Pi Dao (i.e., government faction) and Zuan Zi (i.e., non-government faction) factions, which have gone to extremes. In July of this year, the Central Committee specially sent Chen Lifu to Hunan to inspect and seek a solution. After staying in Hunan for a week and investigating the situation, Chen reported to the Central Committee, which issued four measures on August 6th to resolve the factional strife in Hunan: (1) Executive and Supervisory Committee members Xie Zuyao and others (all from the Zuan Zi faction) should resign without discussion to avoid internal disputes. (2) The Road Association (i.e., the Pi Dao faction's organization for manipulating party affairs), as one of the mass organizations, is still allowed to exist. However, the local party branches should send personnel to participate in and guide the Road Association branches in each county. Any Road Association branches in counties where disputes in local party affairs have already been caused and there is evidence of this should immediately cease activities. Liu Yuehou, the chairman of the Provincial Road Association (from the Pi Dao faction), is one of the alternate supervisors of the provincial party branch. He instructed the Road Association branches in various counties to recruit party members and participate in election activities, thereby losing the position of supervisor who should remain unbiased. This is highly inappropriate and should be seriously addressed to the Central Committee to correct past mistakes. (3) The election of representatives to the National Congress should be handled by the Central Committee in conjunction with the provincial party branch after the above two items have been implemented. The date and method of the election will be determined by the Central Committee. (4) The Changsha newspapers are exaggerating the party affairs issue, creating a bad environment and causing the expansion of disputes. In the future, newspapers run by party members that slander the party branch or attack comrades will be disciplined by the party branch and punished by the government. Other newspapers that provoke negative feelings between the party and the government or cause internal party disputes will be stopped by the government. The above four measures reflect the Central Committee's painstaking efforts to take both sides into consideration and to reconcile the feelings of the two factions. Unexpectedly, in practice, it is still difficult to achieve this, and it is becoming more and more chaotic. The Zuan Zi faction is most concerned about the second item, which calls for the abolition of the Road Association to fundamentally eliminate the Pi Dao faction's organization for recruiting party members and manipulating party affairs. The Pi Dao faction is concerned about the second and third items. In addition to ensuring the existence of the Road Association, they also want to take advantage of the fact that many party members in various counties have been recruited to handle elections and achieve absolute victory, convene the National Congress, elect new executive and supervisory committee members according to the regulations, and create a purely Pi Dao party branch, overthrowing the Zuan Zi faction's power in Hunan's party affairs. The solution formulated by the Central Committee failed to fully accommodate the hopes of both sides, so the dispute could not be resolved. More than a month has passed since the order arrived in Hunan. Except for Liu Yuehou, who complied with the second measure and formally submitted a written reply accepting it, Xie Zuyao and others have still not resigned. He Jian has also not entered the party branch for several months. The executive committee of the provincial party branch originally had seven members. Except for Tan Changkai, who was recalled by the Central Committee and whose replacement has not yet been resolved, there are only six members left. Among these six, Zhang Jiong and Wang Qi (both from the Zuan Zi faction) are serving in the Central Committee, and He Jian (from the Pi Dao faction) and Xie Zuyao (from the Zuan Zi faction) are also absent from meetings. Only Zhu Haohuai (from the Zuan Zi faction) and Huang Jiasheng (from the Pi Dao faction) remain, which is not enough for a quorum, so nothing can be handled. The five supervisors, Peng Guojun, Xiao Fengwei, Peng Yunbin, Meng Qingxuan (all from the Zuan Zi faction), and Liu Baoshu (from the Pi Dao faction), are mostly in the provincial capital, but except for Liu, the others have all submitted their resignations and refuse to attend meetings, so the supervisory committee has also stopped meeting. Hunan's party affairs can be said to be completely at a standstill. Therefore, the party affairs workers, having nothing to do during this period, are becoming restless and starting small newspapers to attack each other. The one founded by the Zuan Zi faction is called "Changsha Zheng Bao," and the one founded by the Pi Dao faction is called "Qian Feng Bao." They spare no effort in slandering and scolding each other, and the "Changsha Zheng Bao" is particularly sharp in its attacks on Executive Committee member Huang Jiasheng. As a result, the antagonism between the two factions has deepened. Huang Jiasheng, extremely indignant, reported to the Central Committee for leave and stated that he would not be responsible for party affairs from the 13th onwards. Hunan's party affairs are not only at a standstill but also disintegrating. Attached is Huang Jiasheng's telegram to the Central Committee:

(To the esteemed Nanjing Central Executive Committee: The provincial party branch, since the resignation of Peng (Guojun), Xie (Zuyao), and other committee members, has been suspended for several months. I, Jiasheng, initially believed that it was inappropriate for the highest leading body of party affairs in a province to be suspended during this time of national crisis, causing a bad impression among the people. Furthermore, party affairs should be promoted in conjunction with military affairs during the suppression of bandits, and should not be interrupted for a single day, leaving subordinates at a loss. Therefore, I forgot my own foolishness and, with my status as a standing committee member, tried to maintain the committee's affairs and waited for your committee to resolve the matter, so that there would be a clear direction to follow. Subsequently, Committee Member Chen Lifu personally came to inspect, and then promulgated a clear solution. I was overjoyed, hoping that the resigned committee members could return to their posts from then on, and that the disputes could be eased from then on. However, for more than a month, the committee's affairs have remained in a stalemate, and have recently become even more degraded, specializing in publishing a newspaper that fabricates facts and confuses right and wrong to attack individuals, especially me. While my own innocence remains unharmed, I deeply lament the decline of party morality, which has a significant impact on the party's prestige. I have the party at heart, but I am unable to salvage the situation. In addition, my old illness has recurred and I urgently need to rest. From the 13th of this month, I am requesting leave to recuperate. I am unable to be responsible for all internal and external affairs of the committee. I am sending this telegram to you, hoping for your consideration.) (September 14th)

The Magistrate of Hua County Begs for Relief 80

The Disaster Area Covers More Than 5,000 Square Li

There Are More Than 300,000 Disaster Victims

Kaifeng Correspondence: Xie Suian, the magistrate of Hua County, yesterday submitted a request for disaster relief to the Provincial Government's Department of Civil Affairs, the Provincial Relief Association, and other organizations. The original petition stated: (The tragic situation in the disaster area caused by the Yellow River flood in Hua County has been reported by telegram. The Provincial Government sent Committee Member Wan Xichun and the Provincial Relief Association sent Committee Member Zhang Tianfang to the county with funds for emergency relief. Special Commissioner Fang of the Third District sent Technician Wang Chaofan to investigate. Inspector Wang Deqing of the Control Yuan also inspected. The association has recently sent personnel to conduct district-by-district surveys. It has been reported that more than 600 villages have been flooded, with only more than 20 villages remaining unaffected. The large dikes in the Fifth, Sixth, and Seventh Districts have been eroded into deep gullies, with mud and sand added to the sides, reaching depths of more than ten feet. As for the First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Eighth Districts, the water depth in the flatlands still reaches from three to eight feet, and it rises and falls from time to time. The water level has not decreased slightly. Although shelters have been set up for accommodation and funds have been raised for relief, there are too few boats and the sand is silted up, making rescue extremely difficult. To this day, most of the villages have not been able to rescue a single person. In addition, there is a shortage of relief grain and a large number of disaster victims. Each person in the shelter cannot be fully fed every day. The disaster victims in the water cling to green trees or lie prone in collapsed houses, exposed to the wind and dew. They long for rescue and have been looking forward to it for a long time. Unexpectedly, Heaven did not show mercy, and the rain continued, causing the water level to continue to rise. The disaster victims in the water are suffering from cold and hunger, and deaths are reported from time to time. They are either drowning or starving to death. In addition, locusts have reappeared, covering the sky and the earth. The crops in the unflooded areas have also been eaten away. What crime have the people of Hua committed to suffer such a calamity? The tragic situation is truly heartbreaking. Now that these disaster victims are orphaned and waiting to be fed and are on the verge of death, since the large amount of relief funds has not yet arrived, we can only raise funds locally. We have selected villages that have not been flooded and have a small amount of surplus grain to provide a temporary solution. We have already raised funds many times, but all sources have been exhausted. Ultimately, there is not enough porridge for everyone, making it difficult to provide universal relief. Now, with more than 300,000 disaster victims, each person needs three "he" of rice per day, which requires 1,000 "shi" per day. The future is long, how can we continue? Therefore, we have to implore the superiors to quickly allocate the relief grain and funds to save our disaster victims from death and prevent them from ending up in the ditches. Furthermore, the breach dug by the Yellow River this time is both wide and deep, unlike other overflows. Even if the water level drops again, it will still be difficult to avoid flooding Hua County. If the province of Hebei does not quickly block the breach, then there will be no end to the water, and it will be difficult to plant wheat for the next season. Long-term relief will be even more difficult. The old and weak will inevitably sit and wait for death, while the strong and cunning will number more than 100,000. If there are reactionaries who incite them, it will inevitably become a continuation of Jiangxi's situation. If we suppress them, the hungry people are pitiful; if we listen to them, the public order will be worrying. At present, there is talk of equalizing grain in Puyang, which is not unfounded. Our Central Government, the Provincial Government's Relief Association, and various charitable organizations are concerned and compassionate. They must have already planned a large amount of relief funds and properly drafted long-term strategies to save the survivors and protect the people's lives. In addition to publicly recommending representatives Mao Binru, Zhang Tianfang, Wang Yaoshan, and Zhang Jingzhou to take the disaster area maps and photos to Beijing and Bianjing to appeal for help, we beg our magistrate to consider the severity of the disaster and ask the superiors to quickly allocate a large amount of funds to bring the dead back to life and save the hungry from the other shore. We are extremely anxious and await orders.)

The situation in the disaster area of Hua County, according to the county government's investigation, is as follows: (1) Date and process of the flooding: On August 3rd, the dike at Shitou Village in Changyuan, Hebei, was breached by bandits, and the water entered Hua County, reaching a depth of three to five feet. It dropped one foot on the 9th, rose sharply again by more than five feet on the 11th, dropped two or three feet on the 20th, rose more than two feet again on the 21st, dropped more than one foot on the 24th and 25th, rose more than three feet again on the 27th, 28th, and 29th, and dropped more than two feet again on the 1st and 2nd of September. (2) Area of the disaster area: Approximately 5,000 square li. (3) Number of disaster victims: More than 300,000. (4) Number of mu of farmland flooded: More than 5,000 square li, estimated to be worth more than 8 million yuan at 1,500 yuan per square li. (5) Loss of property and livestock: The loss of property and livestock is estimated to be worth more than 10 million yuan. Approximately 15,000 heads of livestock drowned, estimated to be worth approximately 750,000 yuan. (6) Number of houses flooded: Approximately 450,000, estimated to be worth approximately 13 million yuan at 30 yuan per house. (7) Number of deaths: Approximately 10,000. (8) Remarks: The total number of deaths is approximately 10,000, and the property loss is approximately 30 million yuan. In addition, the Hua County Party Branch sent an express telegram to various organizations requesting relief, with extremely earnest words, stating: (This time, the Yellow River breached its banks, flooding more than 600 villages in Hua County. The loss reached more than 30 million yuan, and there are 200,000 disaster victims. The disaster is extremely severe, unprecedented in history. The survivors are waiting for relief, which is urgently needed. However, from August 3rd to the present, only less than 10,000 yuan of relief funds have been received from various sources. Using this small amount to rescue such a large number of people is like a drop in the bucket. As a result, those who are calling for help in the water have exhausted their voices and dried their tears, without seeing a single grain of righteous rice or half a bowl of benevolent porridge. Alas, these disaster victims will die before the rescue arrives and will eventually become drowning ghosts. Some who are unwilling to sit and wait for death risk their lives to escape, but die in the mud because they have no boats to cross. Young women mistakenly board bandit ships and commit suicide by jumping into the water. Such cases are numerous. Alas, these disaster victims are either drowning ghosts or starving ghosts. They do not die in the mud and sand, but die at the hands of thieves. Alas, how tragic! The dead are gone, but the living cannot survive without relief. Our association lacks the ability to create money, so we sincerely call for help and wipe away our tears to ask for assistance. We hope that your association will embody the beautiful virtue of Heaven and Earth and spread the benevolent spirit of disaster relief, generously contributing to the cause and universally helping the disaster victims, so that they can be freed from this long-lasting catastrophe and celebrate their rebirth as soon as possible. We are extremely anxious and await your prayers. The Hua County Party Branch kowtows.) (September 11th)

Feng and Pei Counties Hold a Meeting on Blocking the River and Releasing the Dams 81

It Was Resolved to Start Work on October 1st; Contact Teng and Yu Counties to Assist; Xuzhou Circles Telegraph the Province to Request a Halt

Xuzhou Correspondence: Feng and Pei Counties plan to block the Dasha River mouth and simultaneously release the Erba dams to divert the Yellow River eastwards through its old course. This has aroused opposition from Xiao and Dang Counties. Various circles in Xuzhou also attach great importance to this matter. Through the liaison of the Farmers' Association, they have jointly presented a report to the Provincial Peak, requesting that it be stopped. However, Feng and Pei Counties are very insistent on the plan to divert the water. However, since the proposed blocking of the Sha River mouth is in Gaozhai, Dang County, they have not been able to immediately cross the border to act on their behalf. Therefore, they invited Feng, Pei, and Dang Counties to a joint meeting on Yellow River defense. Dangshan refused to attend. Feng and Pei Counties, believing that this plan must be implemented, held a meeting at the Feng County Government on the 9th. Attendees included Feng County Magistrate Yang Liang, Party Committee Member Li Futing, Director of the Property Office Dong Yujue, Director of the Farmers' Association Peng Shiheng, First District Chief Li Xuchen, Technical Director Feng Shouxin, Pei County Magistrate Hu Zhahe (represented by Wu Shijia), Party Committee Member Tang Tongshu, and representatives of organizations Zhang Jingmin, Li Ting, and Li Dayong. Observers included Feng County Supervisor Huang Tirun, Sixth District Chief Han Shaojiu, Director of the Education Bureau Wang Zilan, and Feng County Government Secretary Jiang Sitong. Yang Liang chaired the meeting, and the following resolutions were passed: (1) Should the meeting be postponed due to the absence of the Dangshan representative? Resolution: No postponement. (2) The Gaozhai breach has two channels, the first channel has two sections, each approximately 1,000 meters long, and the second channel is 3,000 meters long. How should they be repaired and blocked? Resolution: Repair the first channel first. (3) Establish a dike repair committee. Resolution: Each county will nominate three people to form the committee. (4) How should the work of blocking the Gaozhai breach be distributed? Resolution: The dike repair committee will allocate the work. (5) Should the provincial departments be requested to send personnel to investigate? Resolution: Request the province to send personnel to investigate. (6) Determine the start and completion dates. Resolution: Start work on October 1st and complete it by the 15th. (7) Should supervisors be appointed? Resolution: Each county will nominate ten people. (8) Estimate the number of laborers needed. Resolution: Feng and Pei Counties will each provide 8,000 laborers per day. (9) How should the materials for blocking the breach be procured? Resolution: The committee will plan the procurement. (10) How should the dike construction costs be shared? Resolution: Feng and Pei Counties will each bear one-half, and request the provincial departments to allocate one-half as a subsidy. (11) Propose to telegraph the provincial government and the provincial party branch to forward to the Central Government a request to build a stone dam to block the Yellow River mouth in Lanfeng. Resolution: Approved. (12) Contact Yutai and Teng Counties to assist in blocking the Gao breach. Resolution: Pei County will be responsible for contacting Teng County, and Feng County will be responsible for contacting Yutai County. Based on the observations of the resolutions, Feng and Pei Counties are determined to implement the water diversion plan and are countering the opposition of Dang, Xiao, and Tong Counties by contacting Teng and Yu Counties to assist in the project. Therefore, disputes may be difficult to resolve in the future. The petition from the Xuzhou Farmers' Association, led by the provincial government and the Xuzhou Garrison Headquarters Special Commissioner's Office, is appended below: (As reported in the Xuzhou Daily on the 11th, Feng and Pei Counties sent personnel to measure the area around Gaozhai Erba and are preparing to mobilize police and armed forces to supervise the work, block the Dasha River, excavate the old course of the Yellow River, and divert the Yellow River eastward. Upon hearing this, we were extremely shocked. The eastward flow of the Yellow River, diverting from the Dasha River to the Weihu Lake, is a natural phenomenon that has been impossible to change for nearly a hundred years. Moreover, the river channel is wide and deep, connecting to the lakes and returning along its original course without causing any major harm. The old course, on the other hand, has been gradually raised due to the accumulation of sand over time and has long been transformed into fertile land, supplying national taxes. Villages and towns are densely populated along the coast, and the commercial port of Tongshan County City and the Jinpu and Longhai Railways are particularly vulnerable. If the water is allowed to flow freely and destroy the Erba dams, it will surely rush eastward, flooding cities and towns and creating an unprecedented catastrophe. Furthermore, Xiao and Dang are resisting and are preparing to fight with weapons. The tragic spectacle of a bloody drama should be prevented before it unfolds. As representatives of the farmers of the entire county, responsible for protecting the lives and property of our people, we cannot remain silent. In addition to submitting separate reports, we are sending this urgent telegram to directly report the situation, requesting that you quickly stop this plan to protect the people and prevent a major disaster. We are extremely anxious and await orders.) (13th)

Li Yizhi Discusses the Fundamental Solution to Governing the Yellow River 82

The Fundamental Project Lies in Reorganizing the Downstream River Channel; Personnel Are Sent in Four Teams to Measure the Entire Yellow River

Beijing Correspondence: Li Yizhi, Chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, went north from Beijing on the 8th to inspect the river works. On the afternoon of the 12th, accompanied by An Lisen, a surveying engineer from the commission, he arrived in Beijing from Kaifeng and is scheduled to go to Tianjin today (the 14th) to attend the North China Water Conservancy Commission meeting tomorrow. Chief Engineer Xu Xinwu arrived in Beijing a few days ago. However, because Liu Ruiheng, Gu Xiangxian, Xi Dejiong, and others are flying to Bianjing today (the 14th) for inspection, he took the Pinghan train to Bianjing last night to meet them in order to discuss everything. According to Chairman Li, he said the following about the measurement of the Yellow River: (I and surveying engineer An Lisen set off from Beijing on the 8th of this month, arrived in Bian on the 9th, and inspected the breaches in Lanfeng and Kaocheng on the 10th. The breach in Lanfeng has been surveyed and can be blocked immediately. Kaocheng is being surveyed. On the 11th, we traveled west along the south bank of the Yellow River, inspected the bridge over the Yellow River, and then inspected the north bank. That evening, we took the Pinghan express train north and arrived in Beijing on the afternoon of the 12th. Because I am weak and ill, I rested in Beijing for two days. Today (the 14th), I am going to Tianjin with engineer An Lisen to borrow instruments from the North China Water Conservancy Commission and transfer personnel to organize a survey team to measure the two banks of the Yellow River and plan the post-disaster reconstruction project. I will also attend the commission's meeting on the 15th. On the 17th, I will go to Ji'nan, but on the 13th, I received a telegram from Nanjing informing me that the Yellow River Flood Relief Association has sent Liu Ruiheng, Zhou Xiangxian, and Xi Mingjiu to inspect Ji'nan and Bianjing. Therefore, I sent Xu Xinwu on the Pinghan express train to Bianjing to discuss everything. The measurement of the dike construction and post-disaster reconstruction will begin immediately. As for the measurement of the entire Yellow River, four teams will be sent out. The first survey team will start on October 1st, measuring downstream from the Zhengzhou Iron Bridge. The second team will start on October 15th, measuring upstream from the Tongguan Pass. The third team will start on January 1st of next year, measuring upstream from the Zhengzhou Iron Bridge. The fourth team will start on February 1st of next year, measuring upstream from Baotou. In addition, there is the Daowei Engineering Office, which is measuring the Wei, Jing, and Beiluo Rivers. This has already begun. The fundamental plan for governing the Yellow River cannot be discussed in empty words. We must have a deep understanding and familiarity with the entire Yellow River, its important tributaries, and the mountains, soil, climate, and other conditions within the basin before we can determine the plan. The fundamental project can only start with reorganizing the river channel and rationalizing the dikes in the downstream area. To control the flood flow and prevent sediment, we must start in the upstream area. For example, the flood that breached its banks this year reached Shanxi on August 8th, with a flood flow of more than 14,000 cubic meters per second. The flood of the Jing River reached the Dazhou on August 5th and the Jinghui Canal Dam on the 6th, with a flow rate of nearly 10,000 cubic feet per second. When it reached the Jingkou Pass, it met with the flood of the Wei River and entered the Yellow River, resulting in a terrible disaster. The amount of mud in the Jing River during the flood period exceeded 50%. It can be seen that if a large reservoir can be built in the Jing Valley to control the flood flow and prevent sediment, then the Yellow River control project will be more than half completed. Other tributaries have the same relationship. It can be seen that the fundamental plan should not be limited to the Yellow River itself. To determine this plan, we must first measure and study the sediment of each river clearly. The Yellow River's measurement and hydrological observation have not been done before, so it will take at least three years to complete. The fundamental plan can also be determined in the fourth year. However, during this period, the temporary projects must still be emphasized to maintain the current course of the Yellow River and prevent the flood from changing its course. Then the fundamental facilities can be effective. If we do not treat the symptoms, then there is no way to treat the root cause. (14th)

Anhui, Hubei and Jiangxi Provinces Request Dredging the Xiaogushan Channel of the Yangtze River 83

丨Jiangxi-Jiangxi Engineering Bureau Completes Surveying and Mapping丨

Wuhu Correspondence: The riverbed of the Yangtze River has been gradually rising due to the lack of dredging for many years. Every summer, when the floodwaters are large, the waterways are blocked, often causing floods and overflowing water, causing disasters. The Yangtze River Waterway Management Committee has repeatedly received requests for dredging and repair from various provinces along the river and local people, but the project is huge and cannot be carried out without huge funds, so it is difficult to implement. Recently, people from Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces, in view of the great flood in the Yangtze River the year before last and the Yellow River disaster this year, once again stated the reasons and requested the Engineering Department of the National Economic Commission to first repair the Xiaogushan section of the Yangtze River channel, so that the water can be discharged without obstruction and reduce disasters, and navigation can be made easier and safer. Xi Dejiong, Director of the Engineering Department, believes that the Xiaogushan Riverway is subject to the impact of Poyang Lake and is within the scope of the Jiangxi-Jiangxi Engineering Bureau. He ordered Lin Youlong, Director of the Bureau, to send engineers to investigate. Recently, the work has been completed. According to Engineer Ke of the Bureau, the Jiangway section is narrow, and Xiaogushan was originally isolated in the river. Now it is gradually connected to the land, and the riverbed has increased greatly. The waters of Hanchuan and other rivers in the upper reaches are blocked whenever there is a flood in midsummer, making it difficult to discharge. As a result, the water level between Jiujiang and Anqing differs by several feet, and the waterways near Xiaogushan are also constantly changing. The Customs Office changes its routes several times a month for safety reasons. In previous years, Poyang Lake could be used for storage, but now the lake has also become silted and shallow, causing mutual harm. Therefore, the principle of dredging should be to carry out both the river and the lake, so as to make a long-term plan. The on-site survey has now been completed, and a repair plan is being drafted and submitted to the Engineering Department of the National Economic Commission for review. (12th)

The Main Culprit in Mengcheng's Drug Case Threatens the County Government 84

丨Li Mingxun Has Been Released丨

Bengbu Correspondence: Chen Zaigong, the perpetrator of Mengcheng County, Anhui Province, who manufactured the drug heroin, was previously released by the Fengyang County Government. The headquarters then sent Geng Zisheng to secretly arrest Li Mingxun in Mengcheng. After capturing the main culprit Li Mingxun and Chen Zaigong fled, Li Mingxun was handed over to the county government for custody and waited to be handed over to the headquarters for legal action. Unexpectedly, after Li was arrested, Li's remaining accomplices bought more than 100 hooligans outside, claiming to be representatives of the people, and rushed to the county government to guarantee Li's release. If they were not allowed to guarantee Li's release, they would rob him by force. Qin Liangzao, the magistrate of the county, and Geng Zisheng, a member of the committee, feared that a major change would occur, so they released Li Mingxun. As a result, the two criminals, Li and Chen, were at large, and their accomplices, seeing that the demonstration was effective, claimed that they must kill the original plaintiff representatives Wang Jianhu and Shao Yabin. They found Wang and Shao in the dark of night, forced them to go to the county government, and forced the county magistrate to take them into custody. Magistrate Qin knew that the local people were strong and feared that a riot would occur, so he temporarily put Wang and Shao in prison. Geng Zisheng learned about this and ordered Deputy Captain Chu of the Security Brigade to lead Liu and Wu to the brigade headquarters, where they were lucky enough to escape. Zhenjiang Cow on Tracks Causes Freight Train Derailment 93

Yesterday at 5:05 PM, freight train number 401, departing from Jing, was about to pass the eleventh telegraph pole at the 247-kilometer mark (between Gaozi and Zhenjiang) when a cow was found lying across the tracks. At that time, the train was traveling at high speed, and the cow was unable to avoid it. The driver was also unable to stop the train in time, causing the train to run directly over the cow, killing it. Due to the cow's height exceeding the tracks, the train's front was pushed off the rails, preventing it from moving. It stopped at the site. Upon learning of this, Stationmaster Zeng of Zhenjiang Station, along with the chief and deputy engineers and Inspector Tian Fuxiang of the machine department, went to investigate and ordered flying squad workers to repair it with all their might. Repairs were completed by 6:42 PM. Therefore, up and down passenger trains were delayed by one hour.

Guo Fenglai's Appeal Still Fails 94

Guo Fenglai, the head of the seventh autonomous district of Zhenjiang County, was previously found guilty in the case of illegally detaining Zhou Rongsheng and Zhou Liu of Shunjiang Island, and was found to have received a bribe from Wang, with conclusive evidence. Zhou and others sued him in the Zhenjiang District Court. After repeated trials, it was concluded that Guo Fenglai had solicited a bribe and was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment and fined 500 yuan. Guo Qin did not accept the judgment and appealed to the Suzhou Higher Court. Three months later, the case was finally concluded yesterday. The court ruled that Guo Fenglai had received a bribe in violation of his official duties and sentenced him to one and a half years of imprisonment and fined 500 yuan.

Prices of Fresh Silkworm Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang This Autumn 95

The Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial silkworm cocoon prices for this autumn have been resolved by the joint committee of the two provinces' silkworm industry control, using 83 yuan of 20/22 silk at a uniform price of 770 yuan as the standard. This includes 250 yuan for reeling costs, leaving a decision capital of 620 yuan. Assuming a yield of 500 silk per kilogram and 290 kilograms of dried cocoons, with an expenditure of 24 yuan per dan, this is approximately equal to a wholesale price of 29 yuan per dan in the market scale, or 35 yuan per dan in the Sima scale. The reeling yield can be adjusted based on the above standard. Yesterday, the Construction Department issued this proposal to all counties in the province for their information.

City News: Wang Jingwei and Sun Ke Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday Morning to Visit Song Ziwen and Discuss Political Affairs

Discussing Enlargement of the National Economic Committee Organization, Wang Visits Huang Fu in the Afternoon Urging Him to Return North Immediately; Wang and Song Are Scheduled to Go to Beijing Together on the Night Train Tonight 104

Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan and Acting Minister of Foreign Affairs, and Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, and others, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:30 AM from Beijing on the night train. Receiving Reporters, Contents of Meeting with Song 108

According to what Wang said at his residence yesterday afternoon when meeting with a group of reporters, he came at the invitation of President Sun to attend the board of directors of the Zhongshan Cultural Education Center. He also planned to visit many old friends along the way. His meeting with Finance Minister Song was to discuss the issue of expanding the National Economic Committee. The expansion of the National Economic Committee had already been decided at the Lushan Conference. The first point was the issue of personnel selection. Chairman Chiang was originally the chairman of the National Economic Committee. Chairman Chiang was deeply concerned that outsiders would misunderstand that the loan for American cotton and wheat would be diverted for military spending, so he strongly requested to resign and recommended President Sun, Minister Song, and himself as standing committee members. As for the selection of committee members, they were originally the heads of the relevant ministries and well-known financiers. It is currently undecided whether additional members need to be hired. The second point was the issue of supervision. It was decided to establish a supervisory organization to exist alongside the executive organization. Mass organizations should also send representatives to join and supervise all uses. The third point was the determination of the uses of the American cotton and wheat loan, which was entrusted to the National Economic Committee to be responsible for the distribution. It was originally planned to be used entirely for production, but now it has been decided to narrow the scope and ensure that it is entirely used for cotton and wheat themselves. In other words, this money will be used to improve the production of cotton and wheat in our country.

Diplomatic Policy is National Salvation and Survival 109

There is absolutely no change in the central diplomatic policy. However, the methods of dealing with it must be based on adapting to the environment. This is a very realistic issue. Since no one can come out and recognize (Manchukuo) or abandon the four northeastern provinces, there is no so-called division between the pro-European and American faction and the pro-Japanese faction. Only through joint cooperation and hard work can we focus on the four words of national salvation and survival.

North China's Finances Maintain Credibility 110

Since the tightening of finances in North China, monthly expenditures still require more than 4.5 million, while income is still less than 3 million. Currently, war-time agencies are being abolished to save expenses, and efforts are being made to increase revenue to make up for the deficit. The only task for Chairman Huang's visit to the south this time, apart from reporting on the aftermath of receiving the war zone, was to visit Finance Minister Song and consult on the financial problems of North China. There has been considerable progress, and Chairman Huang will return to the north within days. Bao Yulin, director of the Beijing Public Security Bureau, has been transferred to the position of committee member of the Beijing Military Sub-Committee. Yu Jinhe, director of the Qingdao Public Security Bureau, has been appointed to fill the vacancy. Director Yu has achieved excellent results during his tenure in Qingdao. This transfer from Qingdao to Beijing was first agreed upon by Mayor Shen Honglie after obtaining Chairman Huang's consent. Furthermore, Chairman Chiang still plans to use Bao in other capacities. Unexpectedly, a movement to retain Bao and reject Yu occurred in Beijing, which is extremely regrettable. Currently, the security in Beijing is temporarily being handled by the district director of the first district, Zhu Ruilin. The central government can express its agreement on this, but will not reverse its decision, maintaining the central government's credibility.

Unless absolutely necessary, there will be no changes to the heads of various ministries of the central government. Huang River Disaster Relief Meeting 113

Liu Ruiheng and Others Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday to Attend

Report on the Inspection of the Disasters in Lu and Yu

The Use of 4 Million Yuan in Relief Funds Has Been Decided

Liu Ruiheng, Standing Committee Member of the National Government's Yellow River Flood Relief Committee and Director of the Health Group; Zhou Xiangxian, Director of the Work Relief Group; and Xi Dejiong, Director of the Disaster Relief Group, and others, were ordered to fly to Lu and Yu to inspect the disaster situation. They completed their tasks and returned to Beijing the day before yesterday. They took the night express train to Shanghai that night, arriving at the North Station at 7:30 AM yesterday. They immediately drove to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Finance on West Aixiens Road in the French Concession to pay their respects to Song Ziwen, Chairman of the committee, and report on the inspection process and discuss relief methods. The details are recorded as follows:

Inspection Process 114

Xi Dejiong, Director of the Disaster Relief Group of the committee, took Euro-Asia Airlines' Euro-Asia No. 8 aircraft from Shanghai's Hongqiao Airport at 6:30 AM on the 13th and flew to Beijing. He immediately met with Liu Ruiheng, Director of the Health Group, and Zhou Xiangxian, Director of the Work Relief Group, who were staying in Beijing, and flew northwest along the old course of the Yellow River from Beijing North, passing through Feng County, Juye, Jiaxiang, Zhancheng, and Jining to inspect the flood situation in western Shandong. They then flew along the banks of the Yellow River, passing through Changqing and reaching Jinan on the 14th. They took off from Jinan and flew west along the north and south banks of the Yellow River, inspecting Pu County, Fan County, Shouzhang, and Changyuan and Dongming in Hebei Province, as well as Kaocheng and Lanfeng in Henan, and arriving in Kaifeng on the 15th. From Kaifeng, they went east along the old course of the Yellow River to Jiangsu, passing through Dangshan and Xiao County, and returned to Nanjing.

Relief is Difficult 115

According to reports, the Yellow River flood this time has flowed and flooded the provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan. Although the flood is not as great as the one in the 20th year, the disaster-stricken area is even more tragic. Because the residents of the counties along the river did not avoid the flood when it came, most of them were swept into the whirlpool. This is because the terrain in the north is very flat, unlike the south where there are high and low areas. Even if there are one or two high places, they cannot accommodate many people. In addition, the Yellow River carries silt, and even after the water recedes, it is still a wet land. There are few boats and carriages, and land and water transportation is difficult. The refugees cannot move and are bound to sit and wait for death. Even if relief supplies are transported, it is quite troublesome. This is why relief feels difficult.

Relief Meeting 116

Liu, Zhou, and Xi went to the Ministry of Finance's office to pay their respects to Chairman Song and report. Song originally intended to hold a relief meeting immediately to discuss relief methods. However, because President Wang Jingwei and President Sun Ke had scheduled a visit, it was postponed until 11:10 AM to begin the meeting. In addition to Chairman Song, Liu, Zhou, and Xi, those present included Zeng Rongpu, Director of the General Office of the Committee, and Qin Fen, Director of the Finance Group. During the meeting, Liu Ruiheng reported on the results of the inspection, stating that the most severely affected areas included 67 counties, and the next most severely affected included 20 counties in Shandong, 11 counties in Henan, and 3 or 4 counties in Hebei. There were approximately more than 100,000 disaster victims in need of immediate relief, and so on. After the report was completed, they immediately began discussing relief methods and adjourned at 12:20 PM.

Decided Methods 117

After detailed discussions, it was decided to establish relief offices in Jinan and Kaifeng, and to request the provincial governments to invite local gentry to organize flood relief committees to work together for greater efficiency. The plan to establish an office in Hebei was canceled because the disaster area in Hebei was far from the provincial capital. The 4 million yuan in relief funds allocated by the government was generally decided to be allocated as follows: (1) 1 million yuan for disaster relief, (2) 1.9 million yuan for work relief, (3) 400,000 yuan for purchasing and distributing seeds, and (4) 1.1 million yuan for health, transportation, expenses, and repayment of advances from various provinces. It was also decided to proceed as soon as possible to save the people.

Written Report 118

The Yellow River Flood Relief Committee released the written report of Liu Ruiheng, Xi Dejiong, and others on the inspection of the disaster area yesterday. The Yellow River Flood Relief Committee, in order to investigate the damage in the various disaster areas, previously sent members Liu Ruiheng, Xi Dejiong, Zhou Xiangxian, and others to Jinan, Kaifeng, and other places to inspect the Yellow River disaster. They have completed their tasks and returned to Beijing by the original aircraft at noon on the 15th. This time, the inspection of the disaster area was carried out along a triangular route. On the first day, they took off from Beijing and passed through Jinxiang, Jiaxiang, Chengwu, and Jining, and then flew northwest to Dong'a and Jinan. On the second day, they took off from Jinan and flew west along the Yellow River, passing through Dong'a, Shouzhang, Pu County, and Changyuan to reach Kaifeng. On the third day, they flew east from Kaifeng, passing through Lanfeng, Kaocheng, Heze, and Dingtao, and returned to Beijing via Xuzhou. In addition to inspecting the disaster situation and taking photos along the way, they also discussed relief matters with the authorities in each disaster area. During the aerial inspection, although they traveled thousands of miles in an instant, they circled over each county they passed through for one or two weeks to conduct a detailed inspection. Therefore, the results were still good and could serve as a basis for implementing relief. Upon investigation, in the Shandong area, such as Shouzhang, Yanggu, Fan County, and Pu County, the flooded land was still a vast expanse of water. In Henan Province, the moon embankments and people's embankments outside the dikes of Kaocheng had been washed away. From the foot of the dikes all the way to the east of the county seat for dozens of miles had been flooded. Countless houses had been washed away, the mud was up to the ankles in high places, and the accumulated water was very deep in low places. The disaster victims gathered in the highest places and slept in the open, a heart-wrenching sight. Changyuan in Hebei, Hua County in Henan, and Pu County in Shandong were particularly severely affected. Although the disaster area south of the Yellow River was vast, the disaster was not as severe as that on the north bank. In total, the area of the disaster area was not as large as that of the Jianghuai River basin in the 20th year, but the tragedy was actually worse. It will also be more difficult to carry out disaster relief in the future. The land routes in the affected areas have become piles of mud, and the waterways lack through-navigation routes and lack ships for transportation. Disaster relief is indeed difficult. As for Hebei, the disaster area is far from the provincial government, which causes many obstacles. Regarding the implementation of relief matters, the three committee members have consulted with Chairman Han of Shandong, Chairman Liu of Henan, and other local officials. This committee will establish relief agencies in Shandong and Henan provinces, and work with local governments, chambers of commerce, emergency relief associations, and Chinese and foreign gentry and merchants to handle the matter. This committee will be responsible for guidance. Relief materials will first be distributed for three urgent needs: clothing, food, and shelter. In areas where fields have been flooded, grain seeds will be distributed. Dikes that have been washed away should be repaired in the shortest possible time. Investigations have now begun to facilitate progress. In terms of work relief, it is planned to first close the breaches, then divert water sources, and build dikes.

Prince Carl of Sweden, having completed his northern tour, returned to Shanghai by night train the night before last, arriving at the North Station at around 8:00 AM yesterday. Prince Carl is scheduled to leave Shanghai for Hong Kong on the 23rd or 26th and depart Hong Kong for Sweden on October 2nd. As for whether he will visit Hangzhou before leaving Shanghai, it is currently undecided.

Native Cloth Movement Conference Opens Yesterday

Native Cloth and Thrift Exhibitions Open Simultaneously 124

The Native Cloth Movement Conference, initiated by nine organizations including the Shanghai Social Bureau, the Municipal Farmers' Association, the Municipal People's Education Center, the Taijiabao Native Cloth Improvement Association, the Shanghai County Education Bureau, the County Farmers' Association, the People's Education Association, the Shanghai Cloth Industry Guild, and the Chinese Cloth Clothing Association, was held at 2:00 PM yesterday at the Minglun Hall of the Municipal Public Education Center on Wenmiao Road. Representatives from various organizations and all walks of life, numbering in the hundreds, attended and delivered earnest speeches. The Native Cloth and Thrift exhibitions also opened simultaneously. The details are recorded below.

Attending Representatives 125

Those attending included Wu Huanru, representative of the Municipal Social Bureau; Chen Kecheng, representative of the Municipal Government; Mao Yun, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Ye Liangguang, representative of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters; Sun Shengzeng and Li Youyi, representatives of the Shanghai County Government; Shi She and Xia Yushou, representatives of the Fifth Administrative Inspector's Office; Yu Zhenhui, representative of the Municipal Farmers' Association; Chen Bai, representative of the Municipal Education Bureau; Shou Zemin, representative of the Municipal Public Security Bureau; Huang Tianshun, representative of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau; Li Zhenshen and Xie Yu, representatives of the Chinese Cloth Clothing Friendship Society; Xu Genghua, representative of the China National Products Maintenance Association of the Penglai Market; and guests Qian Zhongnan, Chen Ding, Ding Zhongtao, Zhou Wei, Wu Zhongyin, and Ma Yuchen, numbering in the hundreds.

Conference Order 126

The opening ceremony was originally scheduled for 1:00 PM but was delayed until 2:00 PM. The order of events was as follows: (1) All stand at attention; (2) Music; (3) Presidium takes the stage; (4) Pay the highest respect to the Party and National flags and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen; (5) Respectfully read Sun Yat-sen's will; (6) Silence; (7) Chairman's report; (8) Speeches by representatives of Party and government organizations; (9) Speeches by guests; (10) Photography; (11) Entertainment; (12) Ceremony concludes.

(Photo by Qichang Photo Studio)

Flag Raising and Unveiling 127

At the entrance of the Wenmiao Road Public Education Center, a banner reading "Shanghai Native Cloth Movement" was hung high. In front of the auditorium, the Party and National flags were hung, and slogans were prominently displayed all around. In front of the stage hung the slogan: "Native cloth can save the Chinese people; everyone should save the country and should wear native cloth." At 2:00 PM, Shi She, representing Director Pan Gongzhan of the Municipal Education Bureau, unveiled the banner and conducted the flag-raising ceremony. The presidium consisted of Chen Kecheng, Wu Huanru, Chen Bai, Zhang Yi, Yu Zhenhui, Chen Songhua, and Jin Xiawen.

Chairman's Address 128

First, Wu Huanru, representative of the Chairman of the Social Bureau, gave a report. Wu stated, "Today is the opening of the Native Cloth Movement Conference initiated by nine organizations in Shanghai. We have initiated this conference with great significance, especially in Shanghai. Why do we need to promote native cloth? Because Shanghai's society, which loves extravagance, luxury, and showing off, has exposed all the shortcomings of the city. We want to make the citizens of Shanghai realize that the rural economy of China is bankrupt and the national economy has fallen into a very dangerous period. If we continue to admire foreign goods and despise native cloth, China will only go down the road to destruction. How can we remedy this? Naturally, we can only promote the native products produced by our own rural areas in China. Among native products, native cloth is the most important. However, the future development of the native cloth industry depends entirely on whether our people are willing to use it or not. If we want the native cloth industry to develop, according to my personal opinion, there are about three ways to expand sales: (1) Native cloth merchants should have the determination to struggle. Although the native cloth produced by farmers is of solid quality and cheap in price, compared with the durable foreign cloth, its texture is not as fine, its color is not as beautiful, and its value is also very cheap. People who buy and use it generally only care about the current beauty and abandon native cloth for foreign goods. Our native cloth stores should have the determination to fight, not hesitate to make any sacrifices, to confront the foreign cloth industry, and persuade customers to try it, so that they gradually know the benefits of native cloth, and sales can be slowly expanded. (2) Native cloth producers should strive to improve native cloth. The texture of native cloth is not as delicate as that of foreign cloth, and the patterns are not as fashionable, as mentioned earlier. Therefore, if we want to expand sales, we must find ways to improve these two points. Native cloth producers should unite and hire knowledgeable and experienced technicians to guide and supervise in order to develop, such as the improvement of iron looms, the widening of storefronts, and the promotion of uses, all of which should be deeply studied in order to be effective. (3) Government promotion and encouragement. The native cloth industry is the only sideline of farmers. At this time of rural economic bankruptcy, the government should do its utmost to promote and encourage its development. The methods are: first, order all subordinate agencies, schools, officials, and students to give priority to purchasing high-quality native cloth for their uniforms to set an example; second, establish a native cloth bonus fund and formulate bonus rules to encourage. In addition, the government needs to help with the sponsorship of native cloth exhibitions and other publicity aspects. In short, the development of the native cloth industry requires the joint efforts of the government, native cloth merchants, and native cloth manufacturers."

Speeches and Entertainment 129

After the chairman's report, seven or eight people, including Mao Yun, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Chen Kecheng, representative of the Nan Government, and Chen Bai, representative of the Municipal Education Bureau, spoke in succession. The meanings of the words were similar and are omitted. After the speeches, there was entertainment to add to the fun. Participants included the harmonica group from the People's Education Center, as well as costume speeches. In addition, Mr. Shen Zhisan and Mr. Zhang Shuzhen, two staff members of the center, performed a double act. Guest Mr. Li Zhaoxiong performed magic tricks, which were quite brilliant and won a lot of applause. The performance by the kindergarten students of Lin Yin Elementary School was also lively, agile, and delightful.

A Glimpse of the Exhibition 130

The Native Cloth and Thrift exhibitions were visited. There were two rooms, designed and arranged by Li Yanqing of the native cloth store. All materials were also supplied by the store. Upon entering, there was a wooden spinning machine. The types of items displayed included various cotton fiber specimens, main cotton crops, insect pest specimens, cotton chemical fertilizer specimens, cotton natural fertilizer specimens, the entire plant specimen of Jiangyin white-seed cotton, the entire cotton plant specimen from the Farmers' Education Center, various native cloth raw materials from the Municipal Agricultural Experiment Field. On the walls were displayed over twenty specimens and charts from the Municipal Garden Field, various three-dimensional drawings of the thrift movement from the Shanghai Municipal People's Education Center, which were quite eye-catching. Other items, such as comparative charts of cotton and rice experiments over two years, showing the yield per hectare, as well as tables of thrift facts of emperors of past dynasties, tables of thrift facts of literati of past dynasties, and family expenditure budget tables, were all of great value.

Representatives from All Sectors of the City to Hold September 18th Memorial Meeting Tomorrow 131

The Municipal Party Headquarters Issues a Notice to the Public

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Maintains Strict Alert

Tomorrow is the anniversary of the September 18th Incident, the national humiliation day when Japan invaded and occupied our Northeast. In addition to appointing Committee Member Jiang Huaisu as the chairman of the meeting, the Municipal Party Headquarters has notified all agencies, organizations, and schools in the city to send representatives to participate at that time and has also printed and distributed a notice to the public. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, fearing that reactionary elements would take the opportunity to cause trouble, has instructed its subordinates to maintain strict alert. The details are recorded below.

Meeting Notice 132

Regarding the matter of notification, September 18th is the second anniversary of the day the Japanese invaders occupied the Northeast. All our compatriots should uniformly suspend entertainment, lower flags to half-mast to express grief, cease work at 11:00 AM, stand up for five minutes, silently swear to wash away the national humiliation, and express deep condolences to the martyrs in the three northeastern provinces, Rehe, the Great Wall passes, Luandong, and Songhu, and the generals and soldiers who sacrificed themselves for the country. Our association will also convene representatives from all walks of life at 9:00 AM on the same day in the auditorium on the third floor of our party headquarters to hold a memorial meeting. A special notification is hereby issued, hoping that all agencies, organizations, schools, and party headquarters at all levels in the city will hold meetings separately in accordance with the above methods and send two representatives with a letter to attend the meeting. A notification is hereby issued for the purpose of the above.

Strict Alert 133

Tomorrow is the second anniversary of (September 18th). Municipal Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hongen fears that reactionary elements will take the opportunity to plot unrest, using the memorial as a pretext to disrupt order. Therefore, he has specially instructed all districts, stations, and teams under his command to implement a uniform alert throughout the city tomorrow (September 18th). On this day, those who have not been approved by Party and government agencies shall not hold meetings or parades without authorization. Those who violate this will be arrested. On one hand, he instructed his subordinates to increase the number of double-person posts on all major roads and streets. In areas bordering the Chinese and French Concessions, personnel were dispatched to carry out inspections. All inspectors and detectives were mobilized for security. It is reported that the police authorities of the Public and French Concessions also have similar arrangements to prepare for any eventuality.

Customs Lianxing Warship Launched Yesterday 134

Customs Secretary-General's Wife Breaks the Bottle

The Lianxing, the largest patrol ship built by the Jianghai Customs, with a displacement of over 1,000 tons, held its launching ceremony at approximately 11:00 AM yesterday. The Customs Secretary-General's wife, Mrs. Lawford, broke the bottle. The details are recorded below.

Stage Arrangement 135

The ship was at the Xipao Pier at Gaochang Temple. A wooden platform of 30 feet square was erected in front of the ship. The platform was surrounded by flags of various nations. A long table was arranged in the middle, with refreshments placed on it. A small round table was also set up, with a statue of an ivory Buddha given by the shipyard to the bottle-breaker. The national flag of the blue sky, white sun, and red earth was hung at the bow of the ship, and a champagne bottle wrapped in five-color satin was suspended with colored silk. Soldiers from the naval guard battalion were responsible for security around the venue.

Participating Guests 136

Those attending the ceremony yesterday included Mr. Chen Shaokuan, Minister of the Navy, represented by Mr. Chen Zaofan, Deputy Director of the Department; Mr. Merger, Inspector General of Customs; Mr. Lawford, Secretary-General of Customs, and his wife; Mr. Jinbo and his wife, representatives of the Japanese Harima Shipbuilding Plant; Mr. Ren Guanghai, Staff Officer of the Training Fleet Command; Mr. Gao Xianshen, Captain of the Haijun Warship; Mr. Lin Zhizhuan, Captain of the Yingrui Warship; Mr. Zheng Yaogong, Captain of the Minquan Warship; Mr. Mao Gen, Chief Engineer, and his wife; the Director of the Hydrographic Survey Bureau; the reception staff, including Mr. Ye Qi, Battalion Commander of the Guard Battalion; Mr. Yu Jianfu, Deputy Director of the Shipbuilding Section; Mr. Liang Xunhai, Director of the Materials Section; and dozens of guests from various places.

The Bottle-Breaking Ceremony 137

The guests were transported by small launches specially provided by the shipyard at the new wharf. At 11:30 AM, the bottle-breaking ceremony was held. Mrs. Lawford held a bouquet of flowers in her left hand and threw the champagne bottle with her right hand. With a bang, Mrs. Lawford forcefully threw the bottle against the ship, and with a loud crash, it hit the bow of the ship, spraying champagne everywhere. Amid cheers and applause, the ship slowly entered the Huangpu River and was towed by two small launches to the shipyard's wharf. Chen, the Deputy Director, then hosted the guests with tea and refreshments.

Director's Speech 138

In his speech, Deputy Director Chen, representing Minister Chen Shaokuan, stated, "Mr. Merger, distinguished guests, ladies and gentlemen, today is the launching of the Lianxing patrol ship. We are honored by your presence and Mrs. Lawford's breaking of the bottle. The Lianxing is the second of the largest patrol ships and is the same as the Dexing launched last time. The Customs has contracted the construction of most of the Lianxing patrol ship (Photo by Weng Peiying).

to our shipyard. Our shipyard will follow the wishes of Inspector General Merger and strive to complete this ship. Now, please allow Mrs. Lawford to accept this small gift, and please everyone drink a toast to the Lianxing!"

Overall Structure of the Ship 139

After the ceremony, Mr. Weng Zuguang of the shipyard told reporters from the Huadong News Agency that the ship has a total of 1,090 tons, a length of 170 feet, a width of 32 feet, a depth of 16 feet 6 inches, a speed of 13 knots per hour, a horsepower of 160, a radio range of 500 miles, and three-pound guns at the front and rear, as well as two speedboats.

| Preparing to Add Fourth-Class Passenger Cars |

The Ministry of Railways' Purchasing Committee previously purchased 70,000 American pine sleepers from Xiangtai Lumber Company on behalf of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. The Ministry of Railways sent Zhang Yuandong, chief of the Engineering Section of the Transportation Department of this railway, to inspect and accept the delivery. It is reported that the Shanghai-Nanjing section urgently needs these sleepers, and the Wusong Materials Factory has notified the Transportation Department to prepare cars immediately and transport 10,000 sleepers to the Shangbei and Suzhou sections for use. The third batch, estimated to arrive at the port around the 17th of this month, will be more than 40,000 sleepers. Furthermore, to facilitate passenger transport, the two railways are preparing to add six fourth-class passenger cars to meet the needs. Gu Xinyi Telegram Requests Additional Tax

On Foreign Rice and Wheat Dumping 143

The Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Oilcake Trade Association telegraphed the Nanjing Executive Yuan's Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "In recent years, the prices of rice, wheat, and flour have plummeted, causing hardship for both farmers and businesses. The main reason for this is the dumping of foreign rice, wheat, and flour in our domestic market. Imposing an additional tax on foreign rice, wheat, and flour is the primary solution to alleviate the plight of farmers and businesses. For months, people's organizations in various regions have been appealing, and the chairmen of the six provinces of Lu, Wan, Gan, Xiang, E, and Yu have been requesting intervention. People from all walks of life are eagerly hoping for its implementation, but it has not been adopted. Then, how can the so-called rural revitalization achieve tangible results? This year's wheat harvest is abundant throughout the country, and the new grain is about to enter the market, and prices are continuing to decline. Blocking the dumping of imported rice and wheat is an urgent matter. We sincerely request that you respect public opinion and implement it quickly to satisfy the people's hopes. It is to be greatly hoped. Chairman Gu Xinyi of the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Oilcake Trade Association respectfully bows."

Chen Wenlin Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 144

Accompanied by Workers, He Leaves for Xuzhou to Repair the Aircraft the Same Night

The Huadong News Agency reports: Chen Wenlin, director of the Naval Aviation Department, flew from Nanjing to Jinan in the Jiangque aircraft the day before yesterday. Unfortunately, the oil pipe malfunctioned near Xuzhou, forcing a landing, and the aircraft body was damaged. Chen arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning from Nanjing. After arriving in port, he went to the aircraft department to visit Director Zeng Yijing and requested that workers be sent to Xuzhou to repair the aircraft. According to Chen, the damage to the Jiangque aircraft was caused by the exhaustion of gasoline in the upper part of the engine, while the oil in the lower part could not be pumped up. When the gasoline in the upper part was exhausted, the engine made a sound. At that time, it was very close to Xuzhou, and for safety, he landed at Sanbugu. However, although the area was flat, the ground was loose and slippery due to heavy rain in the previous days. When the aircraft landed, the wheels sank into the soil, causing it to overturn. Fortunately, the damage was not significant, and it can be repaired in about four days and fly north as usual. After arriving in Shanghai, Chen immediately purchased a new rotor blade that he had previously purchased in Shanghai, along with four workers, and took some repair materials and left for Beijing by car last night, en route to Xuzhou for repairs.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Safety Ordered to Protect Newspaper Reporters 145

Yesterday Issued Instructions to Subordinates

The Kuomintang News Agency reports that the Shanghai Municipal Government, in accordance with a consultation from the Ministry of Interior, has ordered the Public Safety Bureau to earnestly protect all personnel in the news industry. The order reads: (Regarding the matter of instructions, based on the Ministry of Interior's consultation, which was based on the Executive Yuan's Instruction No. 3921, which was based on the Kuomintang Government's Civil Affairs Office's Public Letter No. 3667, which was based on the Central Executive Committee Secretariat's Letter No. 12966, which was based on the Standing Committee's referral of the Jiangsu Provincial Executive Committee's request to order all levels of government and military throughout the country to earnestly protect news industry personnel, etc., which was approved and forwarded to the Kuomintang Government, etc., requesting review and handling, etc., which was then forwarded and His Excellency the Chairman instructed it to be handled by the Executive Yuan, etc., and a letter was sent to inform them to investigate, etc. It is hereby noted that, according to the law, people may not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished, and people have the freedom to express opinions and publish writings, which may not be stopped or restricted except in accordance with the law. Articles 8 and 15 of the Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage have already clearly stipulated this. Now, based on the previous report, the Provincial Party Headquarters has noted that local governments often do not cherish news industry personnel, and in some cases even arbitrarily destroy them, and has specially requested that a general order be issued for their protection, which is deemed feasible. The Ministry of Interior should issue a general order to all provincial and municipal governments and the Ministry of Military Affairs, ordering all military units or military agencies to earnestly protect all news industry personnel. In addition to sending a reply and separate orders, the original report is copied and sent for review and compliance. The original report is attached. (It is noted that newspaper reporters have the responsibility of disseminating culture and reforming society. Therefore, all countries in the world have special provisions for the protection of newspaper reporters, providing them with convenience. China's news industry is still in its infancy. Local governments not only fail to fulfill their duty to protect them, but even disregard legal protections and arbitrarily destroy them, as in the cases of Liu Yusheng and Wang Weisan, which are particularly prominent. Therefore, many people with aspirations in the news industry view the news industry as a dangerous path, and public opinion is depressed, which has a significant and profound impact on society and the public, not only on the news industry itself. For the sake of developing the news industry and improving public opinion, it is necessary to earnestly protect the safety of newspaper reporters. This has been decided at the first meeting of the News Industry Committee of this association, and a report has been submitted to the Central Government requesting that the National Government issue a general order to all levels of government and military throughout the country to earnestly protect news industry personnel. It is hereby recorded and submitted for review and approval, which is a convenience for the party. Respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee, the Jiangsu Provincial Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, Standing Committee Members Zhou Shao, Lan Weibin, and Niu Changyao. It is reported that after receiving the order, Wen Hong'en, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Safety, has issued a general order to all districts, offices, and teams under his jurisdiction to earnestly protect all personnel in the news industry in order to maintain culture.

The Railway Bureau Reduced Freight Rates for Chinese Cement 146

Effective from September 15th, for a period of three months

In recent years, domestic cement has suffered a major blow due to the dumping of foreign goods. The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations consider the China Cement Company to be one of the major industries along the railway lines, with a large annual volume of transportation. In order to adopt a mutual assistance approach, it is proposed to reduce the freight rate for China Cement by 10% compared to ordinary freight rates, in order to benefit both parties. This proposal has been submitted to the Ministry of Railways and approved under Instruction No. 16221. It is now scheduled to be implemented from May 15th for a period of three months, and the bureau has ordered the Traffic Department to comply.

Verdict in the Betel Nut Brand Prize Sales Coupon First Prize Dispute 147

| Manager and Assistant Manager Both Declared Not Guilty |

The Betel Nut Brand prize sales coupons previously issued by the China East China Tobacco Company were drawn along with the Aviation Prize Coupons on July 31st. The first prize, No. 226622, was won by Zhu Wenjiang, a Chinese constable with badge number 3173 from the General Patrol Room. Later, Li Dongtao claimed that he also held a coupon with the same number and filed a lawsuit with the First Special Court when he was unable to collect the prize money from the East China Tobacco Company. The court ruled that Li Xuedong, the manager of East China Tobacco Company, was not guilty. Recently, Zhu Qichang also claimed that he exchanged five Betel Nut Brand hard-shell cigarette boxes for a prize coupon with the number 226622 from the East China Company. After the lottery was drawn, he was unable to collect the prize money from the company and hired lawyer Tang Youwei to file a fraud lawsuit against Li Xuedong, manager of East China, and Li Runsheng, assistant manager, in the First Special Court. The case was previously heard twice by Judge Huang Risheng, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30, Judge Huang continued the hearing in the Fifth Criminal Court. The defendants hired lawyers Wu Lingkun and Chen Zhongyin to defend them. Witness Zhu Wenjiang testified that he had won the first prize for the East China Betel Nut Brand prize. He exchanged the prize coupon at the Dasheng Tobacco and Paper Store at the intersection of Ningbo Road and Sichuan Road. After the lottery was drawn, he verified it with the East China Company on August 1st and collected the prize on August 5th from

Wei Guozhen, a clerk from the Central Trust Company, testified that he handled the payment of the 5,000 yuan prize money and presented the East China Tobacco Company's ticket stub as evidence. After the witness testimony was completed, the lawyers for both sides began their arguments. Judge Huang ruled in court that Li Xuedong and Li Runsheng were declared not guilty, and the related civil lawsuit was transferred to the Civil Court for trial.
