Reports Received by the Sino-Foreign Famine Relief Committee Regarding the Henan-Shandong Disaster 150

The Sino-Foreign Famine Relief Committee, in view of the severe flooding along the Yellow River, has sent personnel to conduct on-site investigations and is raising funds for relief. Yesterday, it received reports from Henan and Shandong, which are particularly distressing. They are recorded as follows:

A letter from the Wuzhi Relief Association states that on August 9th of this year, the Yellow River swelled, and the water level was higher than the embankment, resulting in the flooding of ninety villages southwest of Wuzhi. Houses collapsed, livestock was swept away, crops were destroyed, and countless people drowned. The old and young are living in the wild, exposed to the elements, crying all night, which is unbearable to hear. The first district has a low-lying terrain, surrounded by the Yellow River dike in the south, the Qin River dike in the east, and the Qin River dike in the north. The water has no way to escape and remains a vast expanse of water. In dozens of villages, including Li Houzhuang, not only were the autumn crops flooded, but it is also difficult to sow spring wheat. The people are in dire straits, lamenting at the sight of the water, which is heartbreaking. This is the disaster situation in the southwest. In the southeast corner, the iron bridge and railway run across the area. Over the years, too much stone has been piled up in the riverbed to protect the bridge, resulting in poor drainage downstream. When the Yellow River suddenly rose, the water was level with the bridge, and the water ravaged the area. Houses were swept away. The town of Zhan Dian, more than ten miles from the river, was flooded, destroying thousands of houses, as well as more than twenty villages, including Lao Tian'an and Wei Zhuang. This is the disaster situation in the southeast. In addition, locusts are everywhere, devouring the autumn crops, and there is no hope of a harvest.

A letter from the Yanzhou Catholic Church states that the disaster situation in the southwest of our district, such as Changfen, Dongming, Heze, Chengwu, Wen Shangpo South, Juye North, Jincheng Wuxiang, Yutai, and Yanggu Shouzhang Puyang Fanxian, is particularly serious. The autumn crops have been completely destroyed. Not to mention the villages that have been turned into plains and the houses that have been submerged in mud. Those who died were buried in the bellies of fish, and those who survived were displaced, suffering from hunger and cold, crying everywhere. The general state of misery is unbearable to hear. If it comes to winter, it will be even more unimaginable.

Appeals Must Be Decided by Ruling 151

The Municipal Bureau of Public Safety recently received instructions from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, which stated that, in accordance with the order of the Judicial Yuan, it has been found that when administrative agencies in various provinces and cities handle appeals, they often fail to serve the ruling in accordance with the law and only issue instructions and orders, making it impossible for appellants to file further appeals, resulting in delays and losses. Therefore, after administrative agencies handle appeals, they must prepare a ruling in accordance with Article 10 of the Appeals Law and serve it on the appellant so that the appellant can file a further appeal within the ten-day statutory period if they have any objections, and they must not issue instructions and orders. In addition to issuing separate orders, it is ordered that subordinate agencies comply with this. After receiving the order, Director Wen has ordered subordinate agencies to comply.

Declaration of Donation Relief for the Typhoon Disaster in Southern Chuansha 152

The Southern Chuansha Typhoon Relief Committee of the Pudong Association issued a declaration yesterday stating:

Crossing the Huangpu River to the east, at the end of the Shanghai urban area, Chuansha is to the north and Nanhui is to the south. In Chuansha County, there are three larger sandbars: Hengsha, Gaoqiao, and Yuanyuan Sha. The total population of more than 10,000 has built dikes to form fields, with villages facing each other and the sounds of chickens and dogs audible. The land is suitable for cotton and wheat, and there is a considerable amount of production each year to supply the food for the entire society. On the night of September 2nd this year, a hurricane struck, and the tide suddenly rose. Residents woke up from their dreams to see the flood raging. Climbing on the roofs, the roofs collapsed, and trees were broken. Men, women, old, and young, cried in the wilderness. In an instant, almost the entire sandbar was submerged. Chuansha County Magistrate Li Zihan and the gentlemen of the Yuanshan Hall, including Lu Wenmei, were immediately informed and went to inspect. All the dikes were broken. Some families were missing. Some were more than ninety years old, alone, on the verge of death but not yet dead. Some were three or four-year-old children crying for their mothers. Most were drifting about, hungry and unable to eat, cold and shivering, unable to clothe themselves. The number of those who were buried in the bellies of fish is uncountable. In the reed clumps, people and animals were piled up dead, and the stench was overwhelming, making it impossible to pass. One farmer's wife climbed on the roof, unable to hold on, grabbed a piece of wood, and clung to it until she died, drifting with the current for a day and a night to the coast of Ningbo, where she was rescued and returned home. Apart from this, the number of families who were destroyed and died is unknown. It is estimated that more than 7,000 people were affected by the disaster. The autumn harvest is hopeless, and they will not be able to live on their own until the spring harvest next year. Alas, are those who died piled up and those who survived are barely breathing in the cold wind and rain, in the clumps of reeds and broken docks, not our compatriots of the Republic of China? Are they not our peaceful, patriotic, and productive pure and good people? The clothes we wear and the food we eat, when we trace their origins, all come from their years of toil and labor. Now, those who normally clothe and feed us are dead. Those who have not died are also on the verge of death. Can we close our eyes to their misery and turn a blind eye to their suffering? Can we plug our ears to their cries and pretend not to hear them? Our government and well-intentioned people in our society are vigorously advocating for the revitalization of rural areas and the relief of farmers. If we abandon this most productive rural area, where the disaster is most serious and the need for relief is most urgent, without providing relief, it would be a loss of conscience in morality and a miscalculation in politics. The officials of Chuansha and the local public groups have done their best to provide emergency relief. The population in need of food is estimated at 5,000, with a monthly food cost of two yuan per person, totaling 10,000 yuan. Until the spring harvest next year, for eight months, 80,000 yuan is needed. The number of households without homes is estimated at 2,000, with aid for building houses at 1,000 yuan per household, requiring 20,000 yuan, for a total of 100,000 yuan. Half of this amount is needed for immediate relief. The needs of the coastal areas of the mainland are not included in this. In the coastal areas of the mainland, such as the dikes in the first, second, and fourth districts of Nanhui, which have collapsed, submerging more than 30,000 acres of fertile land, more than 200 houses have been blown down or destroyed, more than 1,000 stones of grain have been flooded, and more than 1,000 people have climbed on roofs to escape the water. To the north, the fourth and fifth districts of Chuansha are largely similar and are still under investigation. The members of this association do not dare to be private about their hometown friendship. For the sake of humanity, we dare to ask benevolent people and righteous people in the world, public and private legal entities, to generously assist us, to save one more disaster victim, to preserve one more good farmer's life, and to maintain one more source of production. Vast floods, floating white bones, living as toiling farmers in the summer fields, dying as flowing corpses in the autumn tide, we use our tears to plead for the release of benevolent purses. Office: Pudong Association, Intersection of Jiangxi Road and Sijing Road, Shanghai. Donation Address: Pudong Bank at the same address. September, 1933, Southern Chuansha Typhoon Relief Committee of the Pudong Association, Du Yuesheng, Mu Ouchu, Huang Renzhi, Shen Menglian, Lu Yuequan, Qin Yanqi, Wang Yiting, Jiang Zhuoyun, Zhang Xiaoliang, Fu Zuoheng, jointly declare.

The World Red Cross Society is handling the emergency relief for the Yellow River flood. The Beijing General Association is coordinating with the Jinan Red Cross Society to provide emergency relief to the disaster-stricken provinces. The Shanghai General Office of the Association received a report from the Jinan Red Cross Society yesterday on the emergency relief situation. The report was very detailed. It is hoped that all Red Cross Societies and charitable organizations will go there as soon as possible to continue the relief efforts. The original letter is recorded separately below.

Report from the Jinan Red Cross Society to the Shanghai General Office of the World Red Cross Society: Respectfully, the Yellow River in Hebei and Henan breached its banks in August of this year, affecting various counties in western Shandong. The eight counties of Heze, Puyang, Fanxian, Shouzhang, Yanggu, Cao County, Juye, and Dong'a were the most affected, with a wide disaster area and a particularly severe disaster situation. The six counties of Jiaxiang, Shan County, Chengwu, Dingtao, Dongming, and Jicheng were less affected. The five counties of Jinxiang, Yutai, Jicheng, Feicheng, and Changqing were secondary. Although the situation is different in each of the above nineteen counties, the people are displaced, the autumn crops have completely failed, and the collapse of houses and the drowning of people and animals are all too common. Although the water has now subsided, it is autumn, and the victims have no clothes or food, and are exposed to the wind and rain. The heartbreaking and tragic situation is extreme. The situation is particularly severe in Heze and other counties. The association regards relief as its duty. When the Yellow River first breached its banks, the Jinan Association immediately telegraphed the various counties of Beijing, Shanghai, Yantai, and Qingdao to coordinate preparations. Upon hearing of the Heze disaster, it immediately invited Mr. Yu Fuhe and team members Liu Miaojue, Xiang Junlin, etc. to carry relief funds and various medicines to distribute as the first batch of emergency relief. It then convened a fundraising conference, and representatives from various associations gathered in Jinan to discuss fundraising. More than 10,000 yuan was collected on the spot. The Qingdao, Yantai, Shanghai, Xichang, and Tai Associations remitted funds to Jinan. Yu Jingsi, team leader, etc., were designated to go to Puyang Shouzhang, and Chairman Wang Biankui and team members Li Yuxiao and Wang Hongzhao were designated to go to Fengpei Dangshan in Jiangsu Province, carrying relief funds and medicines to distribute as emergency relief. Chairman Han Weixu was also designated to go to Dong'a Dongping. At that time, the General Association also sent President Su Jinglin Lu Xuanda and four team members with funds to Jinan. It was decided that Lu Jinxuan from the Association, Jing Weiyi, and two team members would carry relief funds and medicines. President Su and Zhang Suwei from the Association and two team members carried funds and medicines and went to Juye Yang Fan Shou and other counties to investigate and distribute. The General Association also sent President Cao to investigate and distribute emergency relief in the counties under Cao's jurisdiction, and President Nie to investigate and distribute emergency relief in Puyang, Hebei. The above has already been relieved by the Association, a total of ten counties in western Shandong and one county in Hebei. The remaining counties are currently being raised and will continue. However, the disaster is serious and the area is vast, which is not something that a few associations can handle. It is still hoped that various associations and charitable organizations will quickly take action, generously contribute, and work together to save this catastrophe. Attached are fourteen photos of the situation in Heze, which are for your review.

Letter from the Southeast Association: Respectfully, Heaven is unforgiving and has brought disaster again. The Yellow River has broken its banks, and the floodwaters have spread. Hundreds of thousands of victims in the riverine areas of Henan, Hebei, and Shandong provinces have suffered the same tragedy. The people are displaced, and the livestock has been drowned. The old and weak are swept into the quicksand and turned into insects and cranes. The young and strong climb to the tops of trees, barely alive. The dead are gone, but what about the living? The association, whose duty is relief, cannot bear to sit idly by and watch them perish. It has already raised relief funds and remitted them to the Beijing Association. The General Association and its branches have organized a large-scale relief team and rushed to the disaster area to distribute emergency relief to temporarily relieve the immediate crisis and to plan for continued relief. Now that the golden winds are blowing and autumn is coming, the disaster victims have neither food nor clothing, and are suffering from both hunger and cold, making it difficult for them to survive. The association now intends to purchase and prepare 10,000 sets of cotton clothing to be transferred to the disaster area for use as winter protection. However, the association is deeply ashamed of its meager strength and the difficulty of providing universal relief. It can only rely on the great philanthropists to be compassionate and to generously contribute to this righteous cause. Not only will the disaster victims share the benevolence of those who have helped them, but the association will also be grateful for their great kindness. If you are willing to donate relief funds, the association will issue an official receipt to show your great faith. I respectfully submit a brief outline, and I hope that you will give it your consideration.

Sharp Decline in U.S. Far East Trade in June 158

Officially Announced by the U.S. Department of Commerce

The Great American Evening News reports that the local office has received a telegram from the U.S. Department of Commerce, reporting that U.S. exports to and trade with the Far East in June totaled US$53,247,000, an increase of US$11,872,000 over the previous month's total of US$51,375,000. However, it was still 0.2% lower than the same month last year. Among them, U.S. exports to the Far East in June were worth US$20,073,000, a decrease of 2.3% compared to the same month last year. Exports to China decreased from US$5,068,000 to US$4,610,000. Exports to Japan increased from US$6,635,000 to US$7,720,000. Exports to Australia were worth US$2,360,000, an increase of US$353,000 compared to the total value for the entire last year. Exports to the Philippines decreased from US$3,516,000 to US$3,063,000. The value of Far Eastern goods imported into the United States in June was US$33,174,000, a slight decrease compared to US$33,540,000 in the same month last year. Purchases from China increased from US$2,610,000 to US$3,035,000. Purchases from Japan increased from US$8,542,000 to US$11,467,000. Purchases from the Philippines increased from US$8,061,000 to US$10,082,000. Comparing the trade figures for June with those for May, U.S. goods exported to China increased from US$3,749,000 to US$4,610,000. Exports to Japan decreased from US$8,267,000 to US$7,720,000. Exports to Australia increased from US$1,847,000 to US$2,360,000. The total for the first six months of this year was far lower than that for the same period last year, with the total export value decreasing by 22% from US$37,776,000 to US$23,269,100. Among them, U.S. exports to the Far East were worth US$123,786,000 in the first half of the year, a decrease of 31% compared to the same period last year. This is mainly because trade with China has been affected by the fluctuating exchange rates, low silver prices, and the unstable situation in China since the Sino-Japanese conflict, which has made merchants hesitant to purchase more goods. Japan has faced financial difficulties and failed in the neighboring cotton yarn and cotton cloth markets, resulting in a sharp decrease in U.S. cotton exports to Japan. India has also had internal political problems, resulting in a sharp decrease in the sales of U.S. goods.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Customs to Adopt New Weights and Measures 159

So That the Implementation of the New System of Weights and Measures May Proceed Unhindered

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, the Customs Administration, etc., requesting that orders be given to the Customs to adopt new weights and measures. The original text is as follows: To the esteemed Ministry of Finance, Customs Administration, and Ministry of Industry. It has come to our attention that this Chamber previously received a letter from the Qimen Tea Industry Association, complaining that the Shanghai Foreign Tea Traders Association did not comply with the use of new weights and measures, causing tea merchants to suffer unbearable losses, and requesting government support. In response, after the implementation of the new system of weights and measures, various places have been using both new and old systems, leading to commercial disputes, which is not in line with the principle of consistent orders. Therefore, we sent personnel to investigate and found that the reason why foreign tea firms in Shanghai have not yet adopted the new weights and measures is that Shanghai, Hankou, and Fuzhou are major trading ports that conduct business with foreign merchants. They have always used the "pound" system, with 75% converted into Chinese "quan," which is equivalent to 16 taels and 8 qian on the "sima" scale. All customs offices in Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Shanghai are directly under the government and still uniformly use the old "sima" scale system without adopting the new system. The foreign tea trade has direct relations with the customs. If the customs can take the lead in implementing the new weights and measures, the industry will naturally change without any problem. This matter was submitted to the 49th meeting of the Standing Committee of this Chamber, which resolved to telegraph Your esteemed Ministries/Administrations to order all customs offices nationwide to uniformly adopt the new system for all weighing instruments. This is hereby recorded and reported to Your esteemed authorities for review and approval, and we request that you promptly issue an order to comply, so that the new system of weights and measures can be promoted smoothly, which would be for the public convenience. Respectfully, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

"Hengsheng" Ship Damaged in Xiamen 161

Towed Back to Hong Kong for Major Repairs

Cargo Transferred to Shanghai for Shipment to Tianjin

The Jardine Matheson-owned ship "Hengsheng" originally operated on the Shanghai-South China route but recently switched to the North-South routes, sailing directly from Hong Kong, Guangdong, Xiamen, and Shantou to Tianjin. On this trip from Hong Kong and Guangdong to Tianjin, the ship was fully loaded with passengers and cargo, with over 10,000 pieces destined for Tianjin. Unexpectedly, when the ship arrived in Xiamen, due to foggy weather, the navigation was careless and collided with another ship. The "Hengsheng" ship was hit, and the iron plates on the outer hull were ruptured. The damage was also below the waterline. Although there was no major breach, it was no longer able to sail. For the sake of safe navigation and passenger safety, the company immediately suspended the voyage and unloaded the cargo and passengers in Xiamen, arranging for another ship to transport them to Tianjin. The "Hengsheng" ship was towed back to Hong Kong for major repairs. All 10,960 pieces of cargo destined for Tianjin were transferred to Shanghai yesterday and will be reloaded onto the "Dingsheng" ship this morning for shipment to Tianjin.

Page 15

"Shanghai Nichinichi Shimbun" Sends Letter to "North-China Daily News" Clarifying 162

It Has Not Actually Seen a Copy of the Private Letter from Lord Marley

The "North-China Daily News" reports that regarding the Japanese newspaper "Shanghai Nichinichi Shimbun" obtaining a letter from Lord Marley, representative of the Anti-War Association, the editor of the "Shanghai Nichinichi Shimbun" sent a letter to this newspaper last night, stating that the newspaper has not actually seen a copy of Lord Marley's private letter. The newspaper usually tries to confirm or deny news, letters, telegrams, and news agency reports that it receives daily from relevant parties, and this time was no different. Furthermore, it wants to clarify that various information obtained regarding this issue was not obtained with the assistance of the post office or other authorities or government. After receiving the letter, this newspaper informed Lord Marley. Marley stated that he did not wish to comment further on this matter for the time being.

Bandits Collude with Japanese Ronin to Commit Robbery 163

Pre-arranged Automobile Waits at Bank Entrance

Fortunately, Escort Personnel Did Not Arrive; Bandits Dispersed

Police Arrested Them, Handed Over to Court for Interrogation Yesterday

On August 14th, a certain traveler planned to deposit a large sum of money at the Bank of China on Huangpu Road. This matter was learned by bandits Shi Ruichang from Tongzhou and Xu Fengqing from Shanghai. They colluded with Japanese ronin Nishi Eiichi and Hosoya Naoto, explaining their plan to rob the large sum of money. After reaching an agreement, they also invited Hu Hanshan from Haimen, who could drive a car. Thus, at around 8 a.m., the two Japanese each prepared a pistol, lead wire, and towel, and together with Shi and others, hired a car from the Far Eastern Company at No. 1 Pingliang Road, driven by driver Wu Songshan. When passing a remote area of Chunjiang Road under the jurisdiction of the 5th District of the Chinese area in Yangshupu, they ordered the car to stop. The group pulled out pistols, threatened Wu Songshan not to make a sound, stuffed his mouth with a towel, tied his hands and feet with lead wire, and threw him on the grass. Then, Hu Hanshan drove the car rapidly to the Bund on Fuzhou Road and parked, waiting near the bank. By noon, the traveler had not appeared. Fearing that the matter would be exposed and they would be arrested, they dispersed and fled. Driver Wu Songshan was found by a patrol officer at the scene, who untied him, took him to the 5th District Public Security Bureau, and interrogated him about the situation. He was then released. Wu immediately reported to the company, which in turn reported to the police for arrest. Although the Chinese and foreign authorities conducted a thorough investigation, they could not find any clues. The case stalled for a month until the other day, when the Hongkou police obtained confidential information from an informant about the bandits' hideout. Thus, Detective Shi Enjian and Inspector Wang Runhe went to 102 Zhexing Lane, Disui Road, at around 8 p.m. and arrested Shi Ruichang. Then, they went to 18 Haining Road and arrested Japanese ronin Nishi Eiichi, seizing a pistol loaded with six bullets from his person, and took him to the police station. The police chief ordered the two Japanese to be sent to the Japanese Consulate for interrogation, while Shi and others were detained. Yesterday morning, they were handed over to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Local Court. Judge Wu Zehan conducted the interrogation. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the case, saying that although the defendants confessed at the police station, the evidence in the case was still held at the 5th District Public Security Bureau and that accomplices needed to be arrested. He requested a postponement. Then, Wu Songshan, the car driver from the Far Eastern Company, testified that the defendants Shi Ruichang and others came to hire the car, and he drove it. Unexpectedly, when they reached a remote area in the Chinese area, Shi and others threatened him with guns, and the two Japanese tied him up with lead wire and stuffed his mouth with a towel, preventing him from making a sound. Shi confessed that Nishi Eiichi initiated the plan, the pistol was held by the Japanese, and after tying up Wu, they intended to rob the money. When they arrived at the Bund on the Fourth Road, they waited for a long time without success and dispersed. Three days before, they discussed the plan at the Japanese's place on Haining Road. Xu Fengqing confessed that he was invited by the Japanese to help. After verifying the confession, Wu ordered them to be detained and adjourned the hearing to investigate further.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Requests Investigation and Prohibition of Thugs and Vagrants Extorting and Swindling 164

Blocking Cargo Ships on the Caojiadu River

Arrest Those Who Rely on Numbers to Assault People and Rob Goods

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in response to incidents of thugs blocking ships and extorting money or assaulting people and robbing goods in the Jidun area of Pujiatu Canal, sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau requesting a prompt investigation and prohibition by the water patrol team. The original text reads: "To the esteemed Sirs, on the 14th of this month, we received a letter from the Municipal Local Goods Trade Association, stating that recently, in the Jidun area of the Caojiadu Canal, ships transporting local goods have been blocked by thugs and vagrants who extort money or rely on numbers to assault people and rob goods, causing great harm to merchants. They requested that measures be taken to stop this. In response, we believe that the act of vagrants robbing cargo ships and extorting money is a blatant disregard for the law. Therefore, we hereby request Your esteemed Association to promptly request the Public Security Bureau to order the water patrol team in that area to patrol and investigate day and night to suppress banditry and ensure safe transportation. The Pujiatu Canal in western Shanghai is located in a remote area, and if the police force is weak and unable to reach it, how would these people dare to be so reckless? This matter concerns the hindrance of the transportation of goods, and this trend must not be allowed to continue. We hereby request the Bureau to investigate and strictly prohibit those who rely on assaulting people, robbing goods, and extorting money and to apprehend them according to the law." It is heard that after reviewing the letter, the Bureau has already ordered each district and team to investigate and arrest those who rely on assaulting people, robbing goods, and extorting money and to handle them according to the law. (National News Agency)

Chen Yiqin's Home Robbed 165

List of Stolen Items Submitted to Police for Investigation

Chen Yiqin, a native of Wuxi, 45 years old, formerly operated the "Yiji Customs Brokerage" in the Weiwencheng area of Zilai Street in the French Concession. His business flourished, and he accumulated considerable savings over the years. Recently, he built more than a dozen shikumen houses in the Wujia Lane, Houjiabang Road, in the old North Gate city of the Nanshi area. Chen and his family live in No. 5, which is elegantly decorated and somewhat aristocratic, attracting the attention of bandits. At around 6:30 a.m. yesterday, five bandits, dressed in mismatched clothes and speaking the local dialect, suddenly appeared. One of them carried a pistol, while the other two held axes and daggers. The bandits used a trick, shouting "The chamber pot is overflowing!" Chen's maid, believing it to be true, opened the door, and the bandits rushed in, went straight to Chen's bedroom, and forbade her to make a sound. They robbed her of a set of jewelry, a gold locket, four gold rings with stones, two wedding gold rings, a fox fur coat, a gray squirrel female robe, and many other silk and satin clothes. Only a little over 100 yuan in cash was taken. After the robbery, the bandits carried the loot and left leisurely. The victim submitted a list of stolen items to the First Precinct of the Second District, requesting an investigation.

("Jing Bao") Yu Daxiong Sues ("Shiri Tan") Shao Xunmei 167

Yu Daxiong, Director of Jing Bao, recently retained three lawyers, Dong Yu, Wang Yintai, and Tang Mingshi, to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Local Court, accusing Shao Xunmei, the organizer of the tabloid Shiri Tan, of spreading rumors and damaging his reputation, requesting a strict investigation. The main points of the lawsuit are as follows: The defendant's Shiri Tan (a bi-weekly publication) published in its second issue an article titled "Zhu Jiqing Will Also Announce Donations," which stated in the latter part: "(The newspaper reported the other day that Mr. Zhu Ziqiao telegraphed General Li Du, citing Jing Bao's publication of Li's interview, which contained receipts issued by the volunteer army, showing that only 60% of the actual amount was received, and ridiculed it as a 'four-six split.' However, I believe that General Li would never make such a statement. It must be unfounded talk from a tabloid reporter, and the tabloid reporters in Shanghai are mostly worthless scumbags who often engage in extortion. The purpose of publishing this article is for this, not for that." Jing Bao's August 8th news report of the interview with General Li Du was sent by a responsible member of the newspaper and published with his name. General Li Du's telegram to Zhu Qingjia also confirmed this (see the Shanghai Times of August 17th). However, the defendant, in the Shiri Tan published on August 20th, arbitrarily asserted that there was no such interview, affirmed that it was unfounded talk from a reporter, scolded the reporter as a scumbag, falsely accused the newspaper of extortion, and presumed that the purpose of Jing Bao publishing this news was for this, not for that. The 'this' refers to extortion. This can be understood by reading the context. However, Jing Bao has been established for fourteen years. Although its size is smaller than that of major newspapers, it strives for accuracy and fairness in its news gathering and has never used it as a tool for extortion. Even regarding the donation of the volunteer army, it published General Li Du's interview and General Zhu's telegram (see Jing Bao of August 11th) and General Zhu's interview (see Jing Bao of August 19th). If there was even a slight intention of extortion, it would not have adopted such an impartial attitude. Now, the defendant knowingly made false accusations and intentionally did so, which constitutes the crime of aggravated defamation under Article 328 of the Criminal Code and the crime of damaging credit under Article 330 of the same law. He should be prosecuted for both crimes. As for the losses suffered, a separate lawsuit will be filed later." The court, based on the lawsuit, summoned the plaintiff Yu Daxiong and his lawyers to the Second Criminal Court at 11:00 AM yesterday, presided over by Judge Wu Fanglian. The defendant claimed illness and sent a lawyer to appear on his behalf. The lawyer stated that the plaintiff's age and address were unknown. According to the defendant's lawyer, the defendant requested a postponement due to illness and stated that the tabloid Shiri Tan was not organized by the defendant and that the subject of the plaintiff's accusation was incorrect. The plaintiff Yu Daxiong stated that the tabloid Shiri Tan was indeed organized by the defendant and that there were witnesses to prove this. After verifying the statements, the court adjourned and will summon the defendant for interrogation on a later date.

French Police Crack Down on "Blue Shirt Gang" 168

Eight Arrested and Sent to Court for Trial

Recently, robbery cases on the streets of Shanghai (commonly known as "stripping the pig") have become prevalent. A type of rogue youth, wearing blue cloth shirts or blue cloth robes, specifically form gangs and wait in secluded places for passersby. When a person passes by alone, they rush out and rob them. These gangs call themselves the "Blue Shirt Gang" and are led by a leader who distributes the loot. Such robberies often occur in the French Concession in the early morning and evening. Based on reports from victims, the police even received several cases in one day. Chief Detective issued an order to special agents to conduct a thorough investigation in an effort to eliminate the roots of evil and protect the good. At noon on the 15th, French police officers Yuan Zhonghe and Chen Lishun received a tip that a group of robbers would be passing through Jixiang Street on Avenue Edward VII at 1:00 PM to discuss committing a robbery somewhere. The detectives went to wait. About half an hour later, three young robbers, Ye Qingsheng (16 years old, from Ningbo, no fixed address), Chen Fugeng (20 years old, local, residing at 17 Shunyu Lane, Zhonghua Road), and Lin Hai (21 years old, from Nantong, residing at 67 Yanhai Street), came along hand in hand. They were immediately arrested and taken to the police station. They confessed that their accomplices were taking a bath in a regular room on the third floor of the Overseas Chinese Bathhouse on the west side of Xinbeimen Road, Minqiuo Road. The detectives took Ye and the others to the bathhouse and arrested their accomplices Zhang Zhaolong (23 years old, from Suzhou, residing at 22 Fuyou Road), Shen Dongsheng (22 years old, from Pudong, residing in Lan Nidu), Yang Liangen (20 years old, from Tongzhou, no fixed address), Chen Ayu (20 years old, from Haimen, residing at 7 Jiren Lane, Zhengjia Muqiao Street), and Zhang Dexing (22 years old, from Shanghai, no fixed address), totaling eight people. They were all taken to the police station. The robbers were all wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers. After interrogation, they confessed to committing nearly ten robberies in the French Concession. The police chief ordered them to be detained and sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court yesterday afternoon, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo conducted the trial. Police lawyer Yao Zhaodi stated that the defendants were arrested for robbery and that the police had not yet conducted a detailed investigation. He requested that the defendants be detained temporarily and that the trial be postponed for two weeks pending further investigation. After verifying the report, the court interrogated the defendants one by one and then adjourned the hearing until the 26th of this month pending further investigation. The defendants were returned to custody separately. Meanwhile, Detective Yuan and city police detectives continued to arrest the gang leader from Jiangbei, Wu Xiaolian, and Li Changming, near Xiaoshijie, in the 7th of Yangjia Shack Sujia Alley at 6:00 AM. Brought back to the police station, after the police chief questioned them, ordered to be taken into custody to be sent to court for trial the next day, and at the same time, the detective will continue to arrest the gang's fugitives, to bring to justice, in order to eliminate all the roots of the gang.

Hu Xiyuan Discusses the Current Situation of the Light Bulb Industry 169

Electric light bulbs are one of the emerging industries in my country in the last ten years. Since the January 28th Incident, many new factories have been established, but recently, many have been unable to sustain themselves. The truth of the matter is not well understood by the outside world. According to Hu Xiyuan, who is involved in the industry, the manufacture of electric light bulbs requires the expertise of chemical, electrical, and mechanical experts to produce fine products. In 1920, foreign merchants once fiercely competed, causing the market price to plummet. The domestic light bulb industry, except for one or two with thicker capital, barely struggled, and almost no one dared to try again. After the Shanghai war last year, the Chinese people felt a strong stimulus and purchased domestic goods in droves. As a result, the domestic light bulb supply could not meet demand, and enthusiastic people opened factories one after another to meet the needs of the Chinese people. However, during August and September of last year, Japanese bulbs were dumped in large quantities, and this year the market situation is not good, sales are sluggish, and some factories have temporarily stopped production to wait for the opportunity to reorganize. Before the Shanghai war, there were only four domestic light bulb factories, large and small. Now, there are fifteen, producing an average of about 60,000 to 70,000 ordinary bulbs per day. If they can unite, study each other, reduce costs, and improve products, there is hope for the future. Hu also stated that domestic light bulbs must work hard on equipment, raw materials, and production in order to set a low price within the possible range. If they only seek to reduce prices and produce shoddy goods, which leads to a loss of customer confidence, they will all perish together. Regarding the recent price drop of foreign bulbs, he said that it would only provoke Chinese resentment and was not a good policy.

Economist Huang Weiyang Returns to China 170

Economist Huang Weiyang is originally from Shantou and his family has lived in Vietnam for generations, where they are well-known overseas Chinese. Huang returned to China at an early age and graduated from a university in Peiping. Because of his fluency in French, he went to France to study economics at the French National University and the University of Paris, lasting five years. He then went to Germany, Italy, England, the Netherlands, Belgium, and other countries for investigation. He returned to China this summer and stayed in his hometown for a while. He arrived in Shanghai the other day. It is heard that Huang plans to conduct an investigation of the economic situation in major ports in the country and then engage in industry.

Weather Report 181

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The sky will be cloudy or overcast. There will be strong northeasterly winds in the South China Sea and the Taiwan Strait. There will be southerly to southeasterly winds along the coastal areas. The weather is extremely bad in the northern part of the China Sea and the Taiwan-Luzon and Miyako Islands area, due to a violent hurricane slowly advancing east of the Balingtang Strait. The center of the hurricane was about 120 miles within the intersection of 20 degrees North Latitude and 124 degrees East Longitude at about 2:00 PM, moving in a northwest-westerly direction, and 120 miles within the intersection of 33 degrees North Latitude and 144 degrees East Longitude, moving in a northeast-easterly direction. The wind force is unknown. Also, within 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was a maximum of 85.1 and a minimum of 59.7. On the same day last year, the maximum was 81.0 and the minimum was 70.0.

Basketball 190

Shanghai Beats Nanyang Commercial (Men's)

Xia Guang Beats Nanyang Commercial (Women's)

Qianghua Beats Moore (Men's)

The basketball opening games, a total of three games for men and women, were held in the Chinese Basketball Hall starting at 7:00 PM. As the lights came on, men and women, dressed in red and green, flocked in, no less than four or five hundred people. Nanyang Commercial rose unexpectedly, giving Shanghai a major scare. Therefore, the situation was tense and the interest was high, making it one of the most important battles of the night. However, the result ultimately went to Shanghai. The other two games were one-sided. The results were: (1) Shanghai beat Nanyang Commercial 44-31, (2) Xia Guang beat Nanyang Commercial (Women's) 79-8, (3) Qianghua beat Moore 50-29. Details are as follows:

Shanghai Beats Nanyang Commercial (Men's) 191

The Nanyang Commercial basketball team has just returned from a tour of the Philippines. With the help of others, their skills have greatly improved. The wind-swept passing and soft, comforting shooting surprised Shanghai. They were temporarily at a disadvantage, but with a surge of energy, a second decline, and then exhaustion, Nanyang Commercial finally succumbed to Shanghai. The score was 31-43. Looking at the Nanyang Commercial team's talent, they are tall and average, with front and rear offense and defense complementing each other, holding great hope of resisting Shanghai. Therefore, a large number of supporters came to threaten Shanghai unexpectedly. Unfortunately, they lacked the spirit of long-term combat, leading to failure. In the first half, the Nanyang Commercial team was strong and accurate in shooting, with the score often above Shanghai, leading by four or five points, at most winning by 15-9. Under this severe situation, Shanghai worked hard to struggle and gradually achieved a 15-15 tie. Nanyang Commercial paused to find another way. Chen Jinzhi added two points for Nanyang Commercial, taking the lead again. But from then on, the Nanyang Commercial record stagnated. Shanghai's Feng Nianhua pounced like a mad tiger, hitting three balls. Qian Jingguo scrambled like a runaway rabbit, scoring one ball. The score was reversed, and Chen Jinzhi shot two more points for Nanyang Commercial. Lu Zhonghui created a 23-19 first-half situation. Shanghai led by four points. As the second half began, the Nanyang Commercial lineup was scattered and no longer as active as before. On the contrary, Shanghai was in full swing. The veteran Lu Zhongen made a comeback, replacing his younger brother on the court, making the lineup even more solid. Seeing good fortune upon entering, he scored the first ball. Zhao Xikang shot accurately from afar. Nanyang Commercial also scored two points, but the gain did not outweigh the loss. A cup of water could not save a cartload of firewood. Shanghai's momentum was overwhelming, and Wu Guolin's skills became more and more adept, scoring points repeatedly. By the last seven or eight minutes, the game was already set. The situation passed peacefully in a calm state. In the end, Shanghai won 44-31. Referee was Wu Jiatang.

Qianghua Beats Moore (Men's) 192

Starting in the second half, they maintained this situation. Qianghua gradually became more comfortable and eventually entered the second week with a score of 50-29. Referee was Shu Hong.

Huahua Beats Southeast 195

Wang Deyuan

China Wins Robber Cup for Four Consecutive Years

▲ Yesterday, they defeated England 6-0, 6-3, 6-4

▲ Ma Da Takes the Junior Singles Championship in Straight Sets Against Forbes

Today, Four Chinese Players Compete in the Advanced Singles Semifinals 208

Yesterday, China defeated England, winning the Shanghai International Tennis Doubles Championship Robber Cup for the fourth consecutive year. China's Qiu Feihai and Jiang Daozhang easily defeated England's Stokes and Colechu in straight sets, with scores of 6-0, 6-3, and 6-4. In the junior singles final, Ma Da defeated Forbes 6-2, 6-4, 6-4 to win the championship. The matches were all held at the French Chamber of Commerce. There were only over two hundred spectators, making it the day with the fewest spectators for the Robber Cup final in four years. This afternoon, the open advanced singles semifinals will be held at the same venue. All four participants are Chinese, making it the first time in the history of Shanghai tennis. They are Qiu Feihai vs. Yu Tianguang and Zheng Zhaojia vs. Wang Wenzheng. The details are as follows:

Junior Singles Championship - Ma Da's Excellent Performance 209

The Shanghai Open Junior Singles Championship has been won by Chinese players since 1930. The first was Yu Tianguang, the second was Qian Wenshi, and the third was Sun Linfang. This year, there were four Chinese participants. Three were eliminated in the preliminary round. Guo Yujie, the only survivor, unfortunately lost to Ma Da in the semifinals, resulting in the championship being awarded to a foreigner this year. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, Ma Da and Forbes held the final. Ma Da is a strong football player from Las, good at running. He controlled Forbes with ease. His shots and net play were skillful, and his attitude was generous, his swing was natural, skilled, and crisp, and he rarely made mistakes. He is truly a rare talent among new players, but his backhand and serve are relatively weak. Forbes lost three sets in a row, and Ma Da won the championship.

Qiu Feihai and Jiang Daozhang, representatives of the Chinese team that won the Robber Cup for four consecutive years (Photo by Qichang)

Robber Cup Doubles Match - Bland and Uninteresting 210

The Grass Court Tennis Club's Robber Cup International Doubles Championship has been won by China for three years since 1930. In previous years, the stands at the French Chamber of Commerce court were always packed with spectators. However, this year's situation was far from what it used to be. There were only two or three hundred people, making it feel very desolate. The reason for this is that the two English players, Stokes and Colechu, are not top-notch, and China used the aging Jiang Daozhang and Qiu Feihai as a pair, which was not enough to attract spectators. Furthermore, after China narrowly defeated Japan in a five-set battle in the semifinals, it was thought that their final against the English pair, who had defeated the American pair Squire and Smith, would be unfavorable. However, in the match, the English players were mentally defeated, making unforgivable mistakes everywhere, allowing Qiu and Jiang to win three sets easily. This was unexpected, but the performance was bland and uninteresting.

Straight Set Victory 211

After the start, the description was light and simple.

The English players made frequent mistakes, and Qiu and Jiang scored again and again, winning six consecutive games with ease. The total score of each game was 26-11. In the second set, China slipped on Qiu's serve, but then took back Colechu's serve, then took the third game to make it 2-1. The English players showed some edge, applying high pressure and winning two consecutive games, 2-3. It was a flash in the pan, taking the lead. Afterwards, China completed four games in one go, ending at 6-3. The score was 31-25. In the third set, the second and eighth games were quite tense, with many ties. The eighth game had as many as six ties. China won the first two games, and England returned the favor with two games. China then won the fifth and sixth games in a row, and England fought hard to tie it again at 4-4. Qiu and Jiang added two more games to end the one-sided situation with a clean sweep of 6-4. The score for this set was 40-31. After the match, the chairman of the Grass Court Tennis Club, Grimmshaw, presented the award and the event ended.

In the Qiu Feihai vs. Yu Tianguang group, Qiu is undoubtedly the favorite to win. China Education Yearbook Goes to Print 226

The first China Education Yearbook, edited by the Ministry of Education, was completed last month. The ministry contacted various bookstores and libraries in Shanghai to discuss printing. After several rounds of negotiations, an agreement was officially reached with the Shanghai Kaiming Bookstore at 3:00 PM on the 13th of this month. The bookstore will undertake the printing, with the copyright belonging to the Ministry of Education. All printing and distribution rights belong to Kaiming Bookstore. The book is due to be published four months from the date of submission of the manuscript (September 15th, when the manuscript was submitted by the Ministry of Education to the Nanjing Kaiming Branch for forwarding to the Shanghai headquarters). The format is 16mo, with two types of editions: hardcover and popular. The print run is limited to 7,000 copies. The Ministry of Education will unconditionally receive 700 free copies (10% donation of books) and will receive a 10% royalty.

The Navy of Japan, One of the Shenbao Series of Books, is Published 230

The Pacific Ocean is the focus of contention among the great powers in the future, and Japan is undoubtedly a key player in the Pacific. Japan is a maritime nation, and the Japanese are a maritime people. The navy is of great importance to the country's destiny. It is essential for the Chinese people to understand the state of its navy and how it compares to other powers, especially the United States. The Navy of Japan, compiled by Sun Gongdu, is the best reading material to meet this need. The book details the history, geography, organization, personnel, administration, warships, air force, second defense line, and relationship with the Washington and London conferences of the Japanese Navy. The content is rich, and the included tables are especially valuable. It is a must-read for studying Japanese military and politics. The actual price is 3 jiao 5 fen. The special distribution department of this newspaper is issuing it. For the fall school opening, the special price will be for one month. Purchases of 10 or more copies will be calculated at a 30% discount.

China Women's Middle School Begins Enrollment, Wang Xiaoying Recommended as Principal 231

Zheng Hongnian, Wang Xiaoying, and others, together with leaders from all walks of life, initiated the China Women's Middle School and recommended Ms. Wang Xiaoying to be responsible for the planning. The January 28th Incident occurred, and Ms. Wang was unable to leave her important duties in both Beijing and Shanghai for a time. This ideal women's middle school was not realized in time. This summer, the board of directors, considering that the school has been preparing for more than two years and that various circles in the city have been inquiring about it, decided to open the school this fall and recommended Ms. Wang Xiaoying as principal. It is reported that Ms. Wang is temporarily unable to shake off all her duties, so she has temporarily asked Ms. Xu Yuanpu, the former Zhejiang Education Department Commissioner, to be the acting principal. The school has also rented a building at the intersection of Fangxie Street and Linyin Road in Nanshi as the school building. The faculty and staff have also been fully appointed, and the curriculum management is strictly based. This year, only one first-year junior high school class will be offered, enrolling 50 students. A supplementary course will also be offered for students of high and junior high school levels, so that they can have the opportunity to improve their major subjects outside of regular class time. Registration begins today. The entrance exam will be held on the 29th. School starts on October 1st.

Spring and Autumn

Sabbath 232

—Yang Shi

It is said that the one who bestows relics is God. He created the world in six days, using humanity as the mirror of all things, ordered them to be the masters of the Earth, and arranged the Earth perfectly so that humanity could live a fulfilling life, free from worry, strife, and plunder.

After six days, he opened his eyes and looked: Ah! This Earth has land, plants, water, fire, and minerals. (Ah! Good, you humans can now most happily enjoy this perfect gift. You can peacefully be yourselves.) He laughed and shouted, and then, on the seventh day, people began to commemorate and worship him, calling it the Sabbath, repeating week after week. He smiled slightly, enjoying these worships.

However, our God only opened his eyes wide at the time and looked, but did not carefully observe with his heart; perhaps he was eager to enjoy himself and immediately sought enjoyment after six days of exhaustion. So he only opened his eyes wide and thought everything was perfect, and he rested. Look, now, the land, plants, minerals... humans are fighting for them, fighting and struggling. Humans are bleeding, dying one by one. They cannot enjoy this perfect gift. They cannot be their peaceful selves.

Alas, God! Who taught you not to be careful at that time, so that the world you created with your own hands is now completely destroyed? The masters of the Earth, the spirits of all things, whom you ordered, are slaughtering each other. Slaughtering each other, you will have no time to worship you! Are you smiling slightly at this time? I think you must be standing in heaven in despair, mourning for this world. But now I only ask you, don't stand in despair to no avail. Please exercise your supernatural powers and remodel the world. Spend another day of energy, and another week of seven. Then, humanity will not bleed, and truly peacefully be human. Then come to worship you, sincerely worship you, and praise you forever.

Shoe Shining 233

— Yang Yuesheng

Most people in Shanghai like to wear leather shoes. If their finances allow, they will even try to wear a Western suit. Of course, Western suits are inseparable from leather shoes. However, some people like to wear a long robe over Western trousers, which is much more artistic and freehand. Of course, they are also inseparable from leather shoes.

Leather shoes and I have little connection, except on rainy days. Because my leather shoes are a slightly more advanced rough type than the 19th-century (hobnail boots), I am reluctant to wear them. I believe leather shoes are only useful on rainy days.

But I heard that imported leather shoes cannot withstand rain. On rainy days, rubber shoes must be put on. Isn't that not only funny but also quite troublesome? Is it not? Shanghai people are wealthy (and have a craze for leather shoes), and because leather shoes are popular, some people make a living by shining leather shoes. We know that women's eyes often first come into contact with men's feet. Of course, it is necessary to polish and shine leather shoes. Therefore, shoe-shiners are simply indispensable in Shanghai, so this profession has developed rapidly. However, it is a new and moving thing for an anti-Japanese hero to end up shining shoes in Shanghai!

We saw Mr. Jiang Minsheng's conversation with our reporter: (After anti-Japanese heroes arrive in Beijing and Shanghai, they often live in high-rise buildings, have plenty to eat and wear, travel by car, have servants like clouds, sometimes go to Mogan Mountain, sometimes to Suzhou and Hangzhou, and behave extravagantly, which is heartbreaking!) My childish heart died long ago! I don't feel pain, but my head is unusually swollen. But when I think that there are still people who don't admire vanity, don't go to Mogan Mountain, don't live in foreign-style houses, don't ride in cars, and make a living by shining shoes with their own hands, I get excited. I can still see a faint glimmer of dawn in front of me!

Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreigners live together. I imagine for Mr. Jiang that if he were shining shoes on a Japanese person's feet, it seems unnecessary to apply oil because tears can wash away the dust on the leather shoes. As long as your hands don't tremble, a few wipes will do the job.

In Shanghai, there are young heroes shining shoes, and in Liaoning, there are sixty-year-old old teachers being forced to wipe the floor bare-chested. (The Liaoning correspondence of this newspaper on the 5th casts a sigh in contrast!

Random Thoughts on Cartoons丨Who is the Monster丨 234

— Qian Yun writes, Wen Dongliang draws

The alleys are not peaceful. It is said that monsters are causing trouble, and all living people should do their best to bribe ghosts. So some contribute money, and others contribute effort. Even more wonderful and unpredictable is that Mr. So-and-so donated two yuan due to repeated defeats at mahjong, doing business with ghosts, making a great joke.

Who is the monster? Heaven knows, the dead understand, and some people say more frankly: I don't know how many people directly or indirectly maintain their livelihoods for the sake of the Taiping Public Sacrifice. This is still an invisible righteous act. Moreover, most Chinese people, except for this kind of occasion, are willing to spend money so readily. Enough said, then the donors are of course fools, and those who investigate the roots are even more fools. It seems right, but it is not; it seems wrong, but it is right.

If the public sacrifice is effective, I would like to use it to build thirty-three heavens for this society and this country. Wouldn't that be truly immeasurable merit?

Without the popularization of education, don't even think about eradicating things like the Taiping Public Sacrifice!

Cars Crossing the River 235

— Yan

China's transportation can be considered the most complex. And its conservatism is also very strong. Unless forced by the environment, and unable to avoid being backward, one can still see objects from thousands of years ago coexisting with scientific things in the big cities. Like Shanghai's (one bright moon,) its age is at least four thousand years old. Emperor Huangdi created it, or it already had this appearance. It may not have undergone much improvement to this day. But it actually runs alongside the most modern, ever-changing things like trams and cars on flat, smooth asphalt roads. Why aren't we surprised? For example, if someone wearing a square scarf and a monk's robe walks with a friend in a Western suit, what are our feelings? The world is so big, there is nothing strange. The difficulties of inland transportation are even unimaginable to people in Shaoshi. My friend Mr. Jin Lüqin, when he went to Changsha, saw rickshaws in Yiyang with huge canopies that also included the rickshaw puller, like the "oiled carriage" described by ancient poets. If it rains, it is very practical, and the puller will not become a drowned chicken, but it feels a bit bulky.

That's not even strange. Strange things are everywhere, but here it's very different. Because there is no bridge over the Zi River, they must take a ferry. They are riding in cars, of course, they cannot drive straight across, so they have to put them on a ferry to cross over. We remember that somewhere in the United States, trains are driven onto ships to cross rivers. Who knew that the ancient country of the East also has something similar. That Mr. Jin said that he had taken a mountain tram and a cable tram, but this was his first time seeing a car crossing a river, so his poetic inspiration exploded, and he wrote a poem: (Yiyang's mountains and rivers are naturally beautiful, especially with the perfumed carriage and low oil curtains; the most thought-provoking part is when the car crosses the river by ferry.) I heard that Hunan Province also has wood-burning cars and alcohol-fueled cars, so Shanghai, which has everything, is inevitably ashamed of this.

The Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast Army 236

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: The Guest Leaves with Shy Tenderness and a Smiling Face; the Visitor Arrives with Old Grievances and a Sad Heart

Zhao Ziqiang looked at him like that, and couldn't help but feel a strange itch in his heart, so he smiled at him too. Just at this moment, a group of people were walking on the road, and Zhao Ziqiang realized that he shouldn't reveal any flaws in front of people, so he turned around and hurried away. Guizhi leaned against the door frame and stood still, staring blankly at Zhao Ziqiang's departing figure, thinking foolishly. After a while, Mrs. Jiang came out from inside and said to her, "Oh, I didn't look for you enough inside. What are you doing standing at the gate alone?" Guizhi said, "Am I always locked up in the house all day long? I should also come out for some fresh air!" Mrs. Jiang laughed, "Oh! Our young lady is really full of new ideas and can actually say 'come out for some fresh air'." Guizhi said, "The phrase 'fresh air' is very common! What's so new about it?" While Mrs. Jiang was talking to her daughter, her eyes were watching the pedestrian road. She saw large leather shoe prints on the dirt road, going out from her own gate. She thought to herself, "Isn't this Zhao Ziqiang walking away, leaving these footprints?" She knew her own daughter, although she wasn't very stubborn, she wasn't like the female students who talked about love and freedom. Now, seeing this situation between her and Zhao Ziqiang, it was almost the same as talking about love. According to the fashionable people nowadays, couples who have gone through love are a perfect marriage. Looking at it this way, her future daughter and son-in-law will also be a perfect couple. She was always worried that her daughter wouldn't find a good son-in-law, but now it seems that there's no need to worry about her daughter. Mother and daughter stood at the door, staring blankly at the road leading west, a little dazed. Just then, Mama Liu, whom both mother and daughter approved of, happened to pass by the gate and said with a smile, "The weather is still cool, but you two are standing at the door." Mrs. Jiang and her daughter couldn't explain why they were standing at the gate. (189)

Children's Paradise – Patriotic Young Boys and Girls

Italian Boy 237

— Chu

The Italian Prime Minister often said to the Boy Scouts: "If you want the country to be strong, it all depends on you young people. You know that there was a boy who died for the country." This boy was named Barilla. Today, the Boy Scouts throughout Italy are named after Barilla. Originally, the Italian Boy Scouts were divided into junior groups, boy groups, girl groups, and young women's groups. In addition to general education, physical education, and moral education, there were also military education, lectures, mountain forest solitary living, and overseas travel by ship. This is Italy's fundamental cultivation of military-national education, which is indeed unmatched by other countries.

Speaking of Barilla, this boy, sixty-three years ago, when the Austrian army occupied the Italian village of Genqva, armed enemy soldiers rampaged unchecked. At that time, Barilla was very concerned, secretly shedding tears and sighing. One day, enemy soldiers pushed cannons through the streets. The wheels of the cannon carriage suddenly sank into the mud. The enemy officer wanted the people on the street to help him lift the wheels, but the people of Genqva hated that their homeland had been occupied by the enemy and refused to help. The enemy soldiers shouted: "Damn slaves of a fallen country, if you don't obey orders, you will lose your lives." Among them, an officer wearing high-topped leather shoes kicked a villager indiscriminately. Barilla, who was in the crowd, was burning with anger and could no longer bear it. He loudly scolded the officer: "You beast, you are so tyrannical and rude. I wouldn't be content even if I ate your flesh." After saying that, he picked up a fist-sized stone, aimed at the officer's head, and threw it forcefully. The officer suffered a serious injury, and two or three soldiers guarding him immediately fired their guns wildly. Barilla fell to the ground, but unable to get up, he still endured the pain and scolded the officer to death. Thereupon, the whole village shouted Barilla's name: "Barilla, Barilla! We will avenge you!" They scattered and returned home. Even the women at home came with knives and axes, like a raging tide. Seeing the situation was bad, the Austrian army quickly abandoned the cannons and fled out of the village. After this news spread, the people of Italy were filled with righteous indignation. They followed Barilla's patriotic example and rose up one after another, forming a national salvation army to counterattack the Austrian army. The Austrian army was defeated in successive battles. It had no choice but to propose peace. As a result, Italy, which had been a colony of Austria, became an independent country.

Japanese Girl 238

During the Russo-Japanese War, there was a sixteen-year-old girl named Ota Akiko. Her father was a platoon leader. The night before he set off, he returned home to say goodbye to his family. The next day, he left in a hurry. At this time, Akiko had already resolved to die with her father, but because her mother was still alive, she dared not say it openly. Half a month later, her father sent a letter back, saying that he had led his troops to Busan and would soon go to the front line to fight. After reading the letter, Akiko secretly left home and became a nun. She took a train to the Northeast overnight, disguised as a female beggar, and sneaked into the vicinity of the Russian headquarters. Coincidentally, a Russian officer was patrolling outside the camp gate. Seeing that the girl was beautiful, he had evil intentions and took her into the camp. At this time, Japanese Combined Fleet Commander Togo Heihachiro took his flagship Mikasa to Korea. The soldiers of the Second Division had already landed at Zhennampo. Akiko learned the news in the camp and secretly reported the situation in the Russian army to the headquarters of General Kuroki of the Japanese First Army on the Yalu River. As a result, the initial conflict between the Japanese and Russian armies, thanks to Akiko's report, resulted in a great victory for the Japanese army. At the same time, the Russian fleet, which was hindering the Japanese army's plan, was also completely leaked by Akiko. The Japanese army was then able to blockade Port Arthur and cut off the Russian army in Port Arthur and Liaoyang. The Russian army was coerced at both ends and had no intention to fight. Akiko heard that the Japanese army had gained the upper hand and escaped from the Russian camp. She then reported the Russian army's battle situation to the Japanese army. The Japanese army quickly connected the First, Second, Fourth, and Third Armies, echoed each other, and defeated the Russian army's commander-in-chief Kuropatkin's army, occupying the forts behind Port Arthur. At this point, the Russian army was unable to cope. The garrison commander Stoessel begged General Nogi of the Japanese army for peace. This is the reason why Japan won the war against Russia. Later, Akiko died of illness on the way. Her father was promoted to major general for her merit in scouting enemy intelligence. These inside stories are deeply avoided in Japan's official history. However, in Japan's Yasukuni Shrine, there is still a position for a national protection goddess, and women often talk about this story.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Prices Turn Stable 239

Futures Silver and Stocks Decline; London Spot Gold Rises

Since the gold market broke through the 800 yuan barrier the day before yesterday, yesterday's market was still stable. In the early morning, overseas silver markets in the UK and the US rose, the British-US exchange rate rose by 5.75 points, the US-UK exchange rate rose by 3.5 points, the British-French exchange rate shrank by 0.25 points, and the US-French exchange rate rose by another 0.08 points. Gold Exchange forward silver prices contracted by 0.015 and 0.03 points respectively, London spot gold also rose by 11 pence, US cotton and wheat rose slightly, and stocks fell by 2.03 yuan. People's hearts were thus stabilized. The opening gross price was as high as 967 yuan. Although it fell later, the increased spread was calculated on the advanced price from the long side, still rising after the retreat. After the opening, it rose due to the good digestion of banks. Subsequently, the banks took advantage of the high prices to supply. Reuters reported that Holland denied the 1929 covenant to abolish all trade import and export bans, because this move could enable it to fully govern its own economic policy. There was then a rumor in the market that the French gold standard was in danger. The foreign exchange and gold markets turned sharply downward, and there were various rumors of a US inflation bill. However, this was discussed in Reuters' weekly report on the New York Stock Market, and there was no shadow. When the gold price broke through the 90 yuan barrier, those covering short positions were eager, and the banks took advantage of the low prices to vigorously buy. At noon, the situation turned around. The offered price was added to 280 yuan. The mid-day market situation is recorded below: The morning opening was 792 yuan, which was higher than the previous closing. If a spread of 8 yuan is added, it rises by approximately 5.3 yuan. Goods opened at 2.5 yuan. The foreign exchange market opened with a recent selling price of 1 shilling 3 pence 375 for the British exchange rate and 30 yuan for the US exchange rate. At first, it hovered. Later, Mitsui bought US dollars for January at 875, and Fuyu, Hengyu, and Hengxing all advanced. Retail investors vigorously raised the price. The Yokohama Specie Bank bought US dollars for January at 8115. Although Yuanmao, Yongzhi, and Fengyong sold, they were still able to rise. It was learned in advance that HSBC's listing shilling fell by 125, and the US exchange rate did not move. Shanghai bought US dollars for January at 75. Yuanmao, Qianchangxiang, and others bought aggressively, rising to 6.5 yuan. Citibank offered half a yuan for December and fell slightly. Hengyu, Zhifengyong, Yuanshengyong, and Tongyi advanced again. Shanghai bought US dollars for January at 75, and Citibank bought 25 for November, then rising to 7.4 yuan. China-Belgium Bank and HSBC offered 375 US dollars for December, Shunli and Neixing sold, and gradually went downstream. Foreign news was unfavorable, and the foreign exchange market gradually loosened. Mitsui offered 4375 US dollars for December, and soon offered half a yuan again. Many retail investors sold off one after another. Qianchangxiang and Hengyu also sold. China-Belgium Bank offered 5625 US dollars for December, then falling to within 1 yuan. US Cotton Is Driven Up by Inflation Concerns 252

丨The Situation Over the Past Week丨

A telegram from New York on the 15th reported on the cotton market over the past week, stating that the cotton market had turned upward due to renewed talk of inflation. Brisk cloth trading and strong wheat and bond markets contributed to improved sentiment in the futures market, which in turn increased demand for spot cotton. Reports of damage to the new crop and increased boll weevil activity were attributed to recent rains. Statistics suggest that the position of cotton is gradually strengthening, as authorities are currently planning to manage next season's cotton production, reportedly limiting acreage to 25 million acres. Based on the average production over the past decade, the harvest is expected to be around 8.8 million bales. Japanese traders are still procuring cotton in the Southwest. Currently, raw cotton prices are quite firm, but conservatives remain cautious, fearing a slight increase in the movement of new cotton.

Grain: New Short Positions Added 253

Branded Flour Hits New Low Price

The flour market is in a state of irreversible decline, with prices continuing to fall. This month, prices suddenly fell by 2.2 yuan, reaching a low of 2.1925 yuan. Distant contracts were pressured by imported flour and wheat, and various factories aggressively sold, exacerbating the decline. The price of 2.1925 yuan for this month is a newly discovered low. This is due to the current ample supply of flour, sluggish actual sales, stagnant stockpiling, and added new short positions. Manufacturers have no choice but to sell standards to hedge their positions. Buyers can only wait for opportunities. News from Tianjin indicates that standard brands have fallen to 2.29 yuan. Local inventory is high, and sales are slow, making packaging and shipping unprofitable. The closing prices were down 1.5 cents for this month, down 1.75 cents for next month, down 1.25 cents for October, down 2 cents for December, down 1.5 cents for January, and down 2.25 cents for February.

Wheat Futures: Major Players Contend to Exit the Market 254

The wheat market saw imported wheat rise by about 10 cents. Spot wheat supply and inventory were both low, which supported market stability. However, a major player unwound their long positions, while new short sellers sold distant months, anticipating that the dumping of imported wheat and the arrival of borrowed wheat would lead to changes in the market. They sought to exit their positions early to achieve their goals. As a result, various parties covered their short positions after the opening, and prices for all months rebounded by 1-2-3 cents. In the afternoon, competition between major players and new shorts caused the market to suddenly fall again. However, prices for this month did not decline as much as distant months due to the tight spot wheat supply. The closing prices were unchanged for this month, down 1 cent for October and November, and down 5 cents for December and January. The opening price for spot wheat was higher. Fuxin purchased 4,000 bags of wheat from Gaoyou and Yangzhou at the previous market price.

Miscellaneous: Rice and Flour Are Shipped North and South Daily 268

(Yangtze River) There were very few imports yesterday, with only a small amount of tung oil. Therefore, the amount shipped from Shanghai to the Yangtze River is very small. However, piece goods are also likely to have some Japanese goods mixed in.

(Northern Ports) Shipments from Shanghai to northern ports have been dominated by flour, rice, and other food products. Since the invasion, the poor market conditions in the north have led to low prices, which have negatively impacted grain merchants in Shanghai, especially flour merchants. As a result, guest buyers have stopped purchasing. Although a large batch of flour has been shipped to the north recently, it has been shipped by manufacturers themselves for market power reasons, absorbing the losses themselves. Yesterday's shipments to Tianjin included over 35,000 bags of flour and over 5,000 bags of rice. Another 25,000 bags are being shipped out today. The ports of Niuzhuang, Dalian, and Andong are all controlled by Japanese merchants, so there are no further shipments of piece goods and cotton yarn on Chinese and British ships. Imports yesterday included only 1,000 loads of soybean oil from Yingkou. The rest were all scattered.

(Southern China) Buyers from Guangdong and Shantou, seeing that there was a good harvest of rice, have been directly chartering ships to Wuhu to purchase rice. Yesterday, a ship from Niuzhuang departed, and another ship from Ningbo is waiting to depart. Therefore, shipments from Shanghai included only piece goods, cotton yarn, paper, peanuts, and a small amount of flour. Fuzhou was once affected by rumors of Red bandits, and guest buyers temporarily stopped purchasing. The situation has now improved. Today, over 10,000 pieces of flour, rice, paper, hardware, and other miscellaneous goods are being shipped out on the Wanyang ship. Guangdong also received over 2,000 bags of peanuts and over 300 pieces of piece goods and cotton yarn this morning.
