Free Talk

On Attitude 269

— Lin Huiyin

Regarding any matter, people always have an attitude. For example, now that autumn has arrived, some people will express a favorable impression of it, some will express a negative impression of it, and some will have no feeling about it. Those who express a favorable impression will praise it, saying how beautiful it is; those who express a negative impression will criticize it, saying how desolate it is; those who have no feeling about it will say nothing about it, letting it come naturally and letting it go naturally. Praising it is an attitude, criticizing it is also an attitude, and saying nothing about it is also an attitude.

If you are someone who praises autumn, those who criticize autumn may criticize you. If you are clear about your own views, you will not change your attitude of praising it because of that criticism. Vice versa.

If you are someone who has no feeling about autumn, you may be dissatisfied by both those who praise it and those who criticize it. If you still feel nothing about autumn at that time, you can only listen, just as you let autumn come naturally and let it go naturally.

However, if you are a clever person, you don't have to be so rigid, you can be more flexible: when you see that there are many people who praise autumn, you can also praise it a little; if there are few, you can take the opportunity to criticize it. That way you will always be one of the majority, which means you will always be the victor.

Or you may have your own views, for example, you may criticize autumn, but you don't want to admit it openly when you see that there are many people who praise it, because those who are willing to admit it openly are definitely not clever people. However, when you see someone praising autumn, you always feel unconvinced, you always want to say a few words of criticism. You know that you can't say these words directly, you have to be indirect, using them to divert people's attention. You might say, he, that person who praises autumn, doesn't even have the money to buy mooncakes, how is he worthy of praising autumn? After the reaction comes, you can shift the words a little, saying, not being able to eat mooncakes is his own business, why should he come looking for you? Or tell him how to get the money to buy mooncakes.

That way, people can't see your attitude clearly, and may eventually be unable to cope, or unwilling to cope, so you can watch yourself become the victor.

Words of a Bookworm 270

— A Ying

(5)

Song Muzhong (Yunlang Anecdotes) also records: Li Yuhuang Guojin was so poor that he had no money to buy books. Every day, he would take the printing blocks of Confucian classics and histories, caress and read them, making his fingernails black. Over time, he became fluent and became a famous Confucian scholar of his time. Yuhuang was very poor, living in a temple, with only one meal a day. Many nights when there was no fire, he and two old servants would sit together wrapped in worn-out fur coats. Such a scholar (taking printing blocks and caressing them while reading) is truly rare.

(6)

Qian Sigong of the Song Dynasty was born into wealth and could only read. His time allocation for reading was the most interesting. According to him, he would "read classics and histories when sitting, read novels when lying down, and read short lyrics when in the toilet." He was never willing to put down his book. Ouyang Yongshu recorded this. The same record also says that Song Gongchui, when in the History Academy, always carried a book with him when he went to the toilet, and the sound of his reciting could be heard far and wide. As for Yongshu himself, all his articles were written "on the three [places]," namely "on horseback," "on the pillow," and "in the toilet."

(7)

Speaking of Ouyang Yongshu, I thought of Su Dongpo. A few months ago, I read Li Rihua's (Zitaoxuan Miscellany) from the Ming Dynasty, which had an entry about Dongpo copying books. The (Miscellany) says that Dongpo once copied a complete copy of (The Book of the Two Hans). When he finished copying, he was so happy that he boasted that he was like a poor man who had suddenly become rich. Dongpo's high regard for books can be imagined from this. After the (Miscellany) describes this, it expresses the sentiment: Nowadays, people buy printed books, filling entire rooms, yet they do not read them, or they do not read them carefully. Books increase day by day, but learning decreases day by day, and children become more foolish day by day. It is lamentable.

Buying books is a good thing, but buying them without reading them, only to have them eaten by worms or left for future generations to auction off, such a bookworm has no meaning.

English is Not Widely Spoken in Europe 271

— Li Wanjü

The absurdity and outrageousness of Basic English, I think anyone who has read Mr. Lin Yutang's article "Take Away the Hair on My Face" (see the "Free Talk" section of the 10th of this month) will understand to some extent and will not be fooled again. Judging from the articles published in "Free Talk," Mr. Qian Gechuan, who desperately advocates Basic English as an international language, seems not even to have seen that strange book "Carl and Anna," written with 850 words, which is neither clear nor understandable, and makes people laugh until their stomachs hurt. Mr. Qian probably just happened to see some text introducing Basic English in some Japanese publication, and was amazed as if it were a groundbreaking idea, regarding it as a rare commodity. Without delving into it deeply, he hastily brought it to China to boast about it, fully expecting it to cause a sensation. Unexpectedly, it became material for Mr. Lin Yutang's humor, a case of trying to be clever but only making a fool of himself, truly regrettable!

The clumsiness and ridiculousness of Basic English go without saying; and Mr. Qian Gechuan’s act of bringing something he himself did not deeply understand to China to mislead young people, as if he knew what he was doing, is indeed astonishing in its audacity. If this were done by some ignorant monk, we might not bother to comment, but since it was done by someone who received higher education in Japan, it naturally deserves more severe criticism.

As for criticizing Mr. Qian Gechuan and the Basic English he advocates from a scholarly perspective, the authoritative English scholar Mr. Lin Yutang and many Esperanto speakers have already undertaken that task, so I don't want to say anything more. What I want to point out now are a few baseless lies in an article published by Mr. Qian in the "Free Talk" section on the 11th.

Because Mr. Qian wanted to prove that Basic English could be used as an international language, he stated: (Why can Basic English be used as an international language? Because in European and American countries, English is commonly spoken, even in Japan.) And again: (If it can be used in both the East and West, isn't that an international language?) Even if we disregard the fact that Basic English and ordinary English are two completely different things, someone who understands "kiss" might not necessarily understand "lips." Even if we concede that everyone who understands English is extremely clever, and hearing someone mention "the white root that makes your eyes water" they will know it is referring to "onion," is English actually commonly spoken in European and American countries? Can English really be used in both the East and West?

I have not been to America, so I don't know if English is as commonly spoken in the Latin American countries there as it is in the United States and Canada; I have not been to Japan, so I don't know if English is as commonly spoken in Japan as it is in the Shanghai concessions. But Europe, I have been to, and I spent nearly seven long years there. I have traveled to many famous cities and remote towns, and based on my own experience, I can say with certainty that, apart from the British Isles, English is not commonly spoken in other places. Although in touristy places like Switzerland, English is sometimes useful, it's not just English that is spoken there. If you know French and German, you can travel freely without any problems. In other places that attract a lot of tourists, such as the metropolis of Paris, English is not spoken at all. Unless you are a multi-millionaire and can afford to stay in those large hotels that cater exclusively to dignitaries, where there are staff who understand various languages to assist you, someone like Mr. Qian, a petit bourgeois, who goes to such a metropolis and only knows how to speak English without understanding the local language, and cannot find a Chinese student there to help him, will not only find it inconvenient to ask for directions or buy things, but will also have major problems finding accommodation. If Mr. Qian thinks that the ticket collectors, police, shop assistants, etc., on the trams in Berlin or Paris can all speak a few words of pidgin English like those in Shanghai, then he is completely mistaken. Moreover, Europeans highly respect their own national languages, especially those nations like France and Germany who are very proud of their own culture. Even if they understand English, they are unhappy when they see yellow-faced people in their countries speaking English instead of their language, and they will refuse to speak English to you. I think Mr. Qian never even dreamed of such a situation, right?

If Mr. Qian wants to prove that English "can be used in both the East and West," then he should first go to the West and see for himself before speaking. He hasn't even been to Europe, yet he sits at his desk in the editor's office and talks nonsense, using the situation in Eastern colonies and backward countries like Japan to extrapolate to many civilized ancient countries in Europe, thinking that the people of those countries are as proud of being able to speak English as the yellow race are. This is truly a grave mistake!

### New Autumn Miscellany 272

— A Traveler

(Autumn is coming!)

Autumn has truly arrived. The sunny days are still fine, but at night, wearing a cotton shirt, you feel a chill. The newspapers are full of articles about "autumn," big and small: welcoming autumn, lamenting autumn, grieving autumn, blaming autumn... etc. To keep up with the trend, I also wanted to do a little of that, but I just couldn't. I think, even wanting to "grieve autumn" requires good fortune, which is truly enviable.

I remember when I was young, when my parents were taking care of me, the most interesting thing was a little ailment. I couldn't get seriously ill, as that would be painful and dangerous. When I had a minor illness, I would lie lazily in bed, feeling a little sad and a little spoiled, a small bitterness mixed with sweetness, truly like the poetic atmosphere of autumn. Alas, ever since I began wandering the world, my inspiration has fled, and I don't even get minor illnesses anymore. Occasionally, I read famous essays by literary figures, saying that autumn flowers change color sadly and the sea falls silent, but I only feel my own numbness more and more. I have never seen autumn flowers turn color sadly for me; as long as there is wind, the sea is always roaring, regardless of whether I want to be lively or quiet.

A certain lady told us: (Chen is studying science, but at this moment, he completely forgot his interests. All that existed in his mind was to enjoy the beauty of nature to the fullest...) This is also a kind of fortune. I studied science very superficially, having only read a biology textbook, but I can't completely forget those teachings, that flowers are the reproductive organs of plants, that the chirping of insects and the warbling of birds are for courtship, and so on. Last night, while idly in a deserted field, I heard crickets chirping under wild chrysanthemums, and I felt like it was a beautiful scene. Inspired by the poetic mood, I wrote two lines of new poetry:

Below the reproductive organs of the wild chrysanthemum,

The cricket is courting.

Looking at it after writing it, although it is a bit more elegant than the vulgar songs sung by the common people, it is still overshadowed by the poetry of the new poets that comes from "opium withdrawal purity". Writing too scientifically and too truthfully is not elegant. If it were rewritten as old poetry, perhaps it wouldn't be like this. The reproductive organs, using Mr. Yan Fu's translation method, can be called the "sexual organs"; as for "courting," I myself don't understand its etymology, but according to those who are familiar with Shanghai, it comes from Western men and women walking arm in arm, and is extended to mean seducing or pursuing the opposite sex. Courting means hanging, that is, holding each other. Then, my poem translates to:

Below the wild chrysanthemum's sexual organs,

The chirping cricket is hanging an elbow.

Although it is a bit difficult to understand, it seems much more elegant, which is to say, better. People don't understand it, so it's elegant, which is to say, so it's good. This is still a secret to becoming a literary giant. What do you think, Mr. Shao Xunmei and others of the new poet class?

### Shallow Lake (7) 273

— By Joseph Conrad, translated by Shi Heng

He stopped speaking, listened quietly at the door for a while, then shook his head and continued.

(My brother wanted to shout and challenge them—just shout once—to let those people know that we are free-growing pirates, relying entirely on our weapons and the vast sea. But I begged him with our love not to shout. Wasn't I hearing her breath beside me? And I knew that even if he didn't shout, they would come after us soon. My brother truly loved me. He rowed without making a splash. He simply said, "Now you only have half a person left—the other half is with that woman. I can wait. When you become a whole person again, you will come back here with me to challenge them. We are sons of the same mother." I did not answer him. All my strength and all my spirit were in my hands holding the oars, because I was desperately hoping to escape with her to a safe place that men's anger and women's jealousy could not reach. My love was so fervent that I thought if I could escape from the wrath of Indji-Mitta and the sword of our leader, this love would lead me to a land unknown to death. We rowed urgently, panting between our teeth. The oars were deeply immersed in the smooth water. We rowed out of the river; we flew along the canals among the shallows. We rounded the dark coast; we rounded the sandy beach where the sea whispered to the land; the glittering white sand grazed my boat, flashing brilliantly, the boat was flying so fast. We did not speak. Only once did I say, "Sleep, Diamelen, for soon you will need to exert all your strength." I heard her sweet voice, but I never turned my head. The sun rose, and we were still moving forward. The water falling from my face was like rain falling from the clouds. We were flying between light and heat. I never looked back, but I knew that my brother's eyes, behind me, were staring ahead, because the boat flew straight like an arrow leaving the string. No one rowed better than my brother. Many times, together, in that little boat, we had won the race. But I had never used all my strength like this time, this time, it was our last time rowing together. In our homeland, no one was braver or stronger than my brother. I couldn't spare the strength to look back at him, but behind me, I constantly heard his breathing becoming louder. But he still did not speak. The sun hung high in the sky. The heat sticking to my back was like a ball of fire. My ribs were about to come loose. But I still couldn't get enough air into my chest. Then I felt that I had to use my last breath to shout, "Let's rest for a moment!" "Good!" he replied; his voice was firm. He was strong. He was brave. He knew neither terror nor fatigue... My brother!)

A kind of murmur, strong and gentle, faint and weak, like trembling leaves, like swaying branches, passed through the luxuriant depths of the forest, passed over the calm surface of the shallow lake, and the lake water between the pilings suddenly stirred up, striking the thin wood. A warm breeze brushed the faces of the two men, blowing past with a mournful sound, as if it were the short and resounding breath of an uneasy sigh from the land of dreams.

Random Talks After the Leaves

Each Week Worse Than the Last: The Second Anniversary! Public Servant 274

What day is tomorrow? If we are speaking in terms of the total population of China, then I dare to believe that not many people know or remember what is special about tomorrow's date. But we believe that most Japanese and many Chinese in the three northeastern provinces and Jehol have known it for a long time, because all kinds of ceremonies to celebrate the success of the "September 18th Incident" began to be planned a month ago in major cities in Japan and the three northeastern provinces. In the past week, they have even more loudly announced to the public to participate in the promotion: what reviews of the army, navy, and air force! The order of the "September 18th Incident" celebration! Reports on the achievements of the puppet state of Manchuria since its establishment! In addition, there are memorial services to arouse even greater patriotic emotions of hostility and hatred among the Japanese people to mourn the Japanese soldiers who sacrificed themselves for the conquest of China!

Looking back at our own situation, what is it like? To put it simply, everything shows the facts of: surrender, compromise, complacency, forgetfulness, and shamelessness! On the day of the first anniversary of the "September 18th Incident" last year, the government still occasionally expressed its determination to "resist for the long term," and society and individuals did their best to actively assist the Northeastern Volunteer Army and continue to boycott inferior goods. Although the enthusiasm was greatly reduced compared to before the "January 28th Incident" and the Shanghai truce agreement, the spirit of striving was still felt to be largely present. But by this second anniversary—since the North China truce agreement—the scene has changed greatly! The territory lost is even greater than on the first anniversary! The entire territory of Jehol and Duolun Yukai are under the sway of the Rising Sun flag, and the power and strength of the Japanese in North China is expanding day by day. In fact, the severity of the national crisis and the urgency of the environment are many times more serious than in the year of the "September 18th Incident" and the first anniversary, adding many more difficult facts. However, this more serious and difficult situation has instead made the attitude of our government and people leisurely. Everything that was loudly called for in the past—resistance, economic severance—seems to be gradually fading and vanishing. The salaries of government personnel have returned to the state before the "September 18th Incident," which can also be said to be a longer and more enduring expression of "long-term resistance" and "bearing humiliation and carrying heavy burdens"? As for our people, most of the anti-Japanese generals who led the Volunteer Army in the Northeast in the past have been forced to flee into the customs. The existing Volunteer Army also cannot carry out large-scale resistance due to the decreasing supply of relief. The only weapon held by the general public—boycotting inferior goods—cannot be insisted upon. Alas! Looking at the past and comparing it to the present, it truly makes people feel that this unprecedented "September 18th Incident" national disaster anniversary is truly getting worse every year!

Some people say: "Human nature is forgetful, and ignorant and inferior nations are even more forgetful." Although we Chinese are disappointing, if we do not admit that we are an "ignorant and inferior" nation, then how should we strive to awaken and break the silent status quo of whitewashing peace in the increasingly serious environment of national and international disasters in the future? We must deeply understand that the current silent status quo is also the status quo of national subjugation and racial extinction. If things continue like this, getting worse every year, the result will only be to become slaves to a conquered country, at the mercy of others!

Look! Our enemies, how are they building up their military and preparing for a second world war in a down-to-earth manner? If we have the ambition to save the country and the determination to kill the enemy, then in the future, whether it is the government or the people, we should show it to others through practical actions. This is our only hope for commemorating the second anniversary of the "September 18th Incident." Otherwise, if we only talk empty words of long-term resistance or play some half-hearted tricks of boycotting inferior goods, then, to put it bluntly, this is tantamount to "selling out the people" and "flattering the enemy"!

Life (Carelessness) Wang Dake

### Dock Coolie 275

Every day, when the morning light is faint, I spend twelve copper coins to buy two pairs of worker's (ingots candles) (two large pancakes sandwiched with two fried dough sticks), eat them, and then set off towards the Bailianjing XX dock. The ships, great and magnificent presidential ships loaded with foreign goods, are moored like mountains along the edge of the dock.

Six o'clock has already struck. After Song Xiaosanzi calls the roll like a platoon leader, the coolie (i.e., worker) life of (the devil is calling you poor! Endure it hard!) begins again. The "Wenzhi" (goods warehouse) winches one load after another from the ship's cargo hold to the dock, piles of goods: cotton, wheat flour, Oriental salted fish, cars, airplanes... all moved to the cement on the dock. Our fellow workers, some use trolleys, pushing them load after load into the cargo hold, some carry them on their shoulders one load at a time, some carry them together with two people, also on their shoulders, and some push and pull them together with four, six, or eight people, all going towards the warehouse. However, soon, their hands are scratched and bleeding, and their shoulders quickly become red, swollen, and painful. However, these are all minor matters. In the bottom of the ship's cargo hold, under the "Wenzhi," and when moving on the swaying gangplank, this is where there is the greatest danger to life, but who cares about it? Like the time the pre-water ship, the World Class XX Presidential Ship, arrived, our fellow worker, Xiao Fuzi, fell from the deck (carelessly) (?) into the cargo hold, and immediately suffered the misfortune of being crushed to pieces, alas! His death was truly tragic! But who cares about it? Ask the company for compensation? But they will answer you like this: (This has nothing to do with our company. His "carelessness" is not the responsibility of our company. But the company is very "sorry" for his misfortune...). The sun has reached the center, and the fierce light shines down like fire, baking our backs like Cantonese roasted pig skin. It's time for lunch, each person deducts four hundred cash, coarse No. 4 rice, winter melon and tofu soup, a dish of salted radish, alas! We (coolies), low-class people, are only worthy of eating such food.

One o'clock in the afternoon has arrived. The "Wenzhi" roars again, no matter how red and swollen your shoulders are, no matter how painful, you must never rest, otherwise the foreman's fist will immediately be sent to your chest, and even your day's wages will be confiscated (actually, it goes into the foreman's own pocket). Like this, until the sun sets in the west, at six o'clock, by which time the cargo hold is piled high with goods like a small mountain, our work is considered to be one day's work. Then our "old friend" Xiao Sanzi issues us a bamboo slip like the gentlemen in the refugee camp, and in addition to deducting four hundred cash for lunch, you can also get one thousand two hundred cash from the old man's house.

(Isn't it one dollar and forty-five cents a day?) After receiving my wages with the bamboo slip, I asked one of our fellow workers. He looked around and then replied to me: (Where is there such a good world? Alas! Old brother—in the past, the company issued one dollar and eighty-five cents a day, but now it has been reduced by forty cents, and it is all judged by the contractor, and after one judgment, two judgments, three judgments... Old brother, that's right—one dollar and forty-five cents a day, the first judgment takes away forty cents, the second judgment takes away twenty cents, and the third judgment also takes away twenty cents. After the stripping and drawing, isn't there only one string and six hundred cash left?) After hearing these words, I suddenly felt enlightened. I stroked my red and swollen shoulders, but could only swallow a sigh that I dared not utter. Then I thought again: we will only have work to do when the ship arrives next Monday, but what about life?
